But the live PS-320-v2 run (v0.99.92) surfaced the **other face** of the same storage-auto-grow event: the target's **binlog volume hit `errno 28` (No space left on device)** during the grow → target replica SQL thread failed → under semi-sync the target primary's writes **STALLED (blocked, not errored)** → sluice's pipeline backpressured → the **source** read connection went idle past the source's `net_write_timeout` (60 s) → the source closed it (`unexpected EOF`/`invalid connection`) → cold-copy aborted on the SOURCE side. ADR-0108 can't catch a write that *blocks*, and the first error was on the read side — so the source-read path needs its own resilience.

**What (shipped, three-pronged — corrected from the first design once the sync consistent-snapshot constraint surfaced: MySQL can't re-establish a frozen snapshot on a fresh connection, so per-table resume is `migrate`-only).** **(A, primary)** raise `net_write_timeout`/`net_read_timeout` to a bounded ~10-min default on every MySQL source read session (DSN-param at handshake; operator override wins) so a transient target stall no longer drops the idle source read. **(B, sync backstop)** a source-read drop during the cold-copy phase (no CDC anchor yet) bounded-auto-restarts the cold-start via the v0.99.73 force-fresh path (drop+recreate for native plain, UPSERT for idempotent) instead of fatal-exiting; once a CDC anchor exists it warm-resumes (unchanged). **(C, `migrate` path)** per-table reconnect+resume from `chunk.LastPK` (keyset) or truncate-restart (non-chunkable). MySQL-scoped; PG `COPY`-source = follow-up.

**Gotchas (carried).** (1) The `(B)` discriminator MUST be airtight — only force a re-copy when there is no durable CDC progress (no `cdc_state` anchor), else a re-copy would clobber CDC progress. (2) Bound everything (the (A) timeout finite; (B) on the apply-retry budget) so a genuinely-dead target still surfaces. (3) Live re-validation needs a FRESH small-volume non-Metal target so the 10→39 GB grow re-triggers the binlog-fill stall — a pre-grown volume won't reproduce it.

### 35. Persist polled PlanetScale metrics as a rolling history (current / 1 min / 5 min / 10 min) in a sluice metadata table — *operator-flagged 2026-06-21; extends item 32 / ADR-0107* — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.107** (engine-neutral `ir.TargetMetricsHistoryStore` seam + MySQL & Postgres stores; `sluice_target_metrics_history` table on the target; pipeline recorder sidecar mirroring the storage-headroom watch [60 s dedupe-by-SampledAt, 7-day TTL prune, fully failure-isolated]; `health/target_metrics_history.json` diagnose section with current/1m/5m/10m avg+max; default-on when telemetry configured, `--suppress-target-metrics-history` opt-out; NULL⇄*Known honesty contract single-sourced in `ir`)

**Why.** Item-32 Phase 1's `TargetHealthSnapshot` is point-in-time + in-memory (consumed by the AIMD damp + the storage WARN, exported as instantaneous `sluice_target_*` gauges). Operators frequently want the metrics PlanetScale shows in its UI **without** scripting the metrics API themselves — and they want *trend* (is CPU climbing? did storage just step?), not just the instant value. Persisting a short rolling history in sluice's own metadata makes that a `SELECT` (or a `sluice diagnose` panel) instead of an API integration.

**What.** When the Phase-2 PlanetScale provider (item 32) is wired, also write each poll into a bounded metadata table (e.g. `sluice_target_metrics_history`: ts, branch/db, cpu/mem/storage util, raw volume bytes, lag, conns) and/or maintain rolling aggregates (current, last-1m, last-5m, last-10m avg/max) so `sluice diagnose` / a query surfaces the recent trend. Keep it bounded (ring-buffer / TTL prune — don't grow unbounded). Refresh cadence is gated by the PlanetScale scrape interval (the SD targets advertise `__scrape_interval__=1m` / `__scrape_timeout__=20s`, so the underlying data only updates ~once a minute — sluice should align its persisted cadence to ~60s and not imply finer resolution than the source provides; dedupe by the sample's embedded timestamp). Pairs with ADR-0107's split-out "export sluice's own richer `/metrics`" sub-item.

**Gotchas.** (1) Bounded storage + prune (never an unbounded history table). (2) Don't fabricate resolution finer than PS's ~1-min scrape — label the cadence honestly. (3) Engine-neutral metadata shape; the PS-specific provider fills it, the table contract stays generic (other providers could populate it).

### 36. `sluice` metrics-watch / notification mode — poll target metrics and funnel threshold alerts to Slack / email / generic webhook (operator-flagged 2026-06-21) — **✅ in-sync alerter SHIPPED v0.99.108** (engine-neutral `internal/notify` sink layer: generic webhook + Slack incoming-webhook, credential-gated via `SLUICE_NOTIFY_WEBHOOK`/`SLUICE_NOTIFY_SLACK`; pipeline threshold-alerter sidecar with edge-trigger + per-rule cooldown [`--notify-cooldown` 15m] + hysteresis re-arm; rules `--notify-storage-util`/`-cpu-util`/`-mem-util`/`-lag-seconds` + rate-of-change `--notify-storage-growth-per-min`; failure-isolated [dead sink logged+swallowed], unobserved-metric-never-fires; opt-in, telemetry-gated. **Standalone `metrics-watch` daemon SHIPPED v0.99.115** (framing (b)): `sluice metrics-watch --engine --planetscale-org --planetscale-metrics-db` polls a PS database's control-plane metrics with NO sync/DB-connection attached, prints a live `cpu=/mem=/storage=/lag=/conns=` line, and fires the SAME edge-trigger+cooldown+hysteresis alerts [shared `buildMetricsNotifyRulesFrom`/`runMetricsNotifyTick` — can't drift from the sync path]; `--once`/`--quiet`/`--interval`; optional `--metrics-listen` makes it a standalone PS-metrics Prometheus exporter [see item 32]. **Only the SMTP/email sink stays demand-gated** [the generic webhook + Slack cover email via the user's own relay].)

**Why.** Operators most often want to be **notified** off metrics — "tell me when CPU/mem/storage crosses X," "warn me before a storage auto-grow," "alert if replica lag spikes." PlanetScale's webhooks are **event**-based (deploy requests, branch lifecycle, etc.), not **metric-threshold**-based, so this need is currently unmet. sluice already polls + distills the metrics (item 32); a thin watch/alert layer on top is a natural, high-demand capability.

**What.** An optional operating mode (e.g. `sluice metrics watch` / a `--notify` sink on a running sync) that evaluates the polled `TargetHealthSnapshot` against operator-set thresholds and emits to pluggable **notification sinks** — Slack (incoming webhook), email (SMTP), and a **generic webhook/JSON-POST** (so users can fan out to anything). Edge-triggered + de-duplicated (one alert per crossing, not per poll — mirror the item-32 storage-WARN edge logic) with a re-arm/cooldown. Two framings to decide in the ADR: **(a) sync-scoped** — alerts ride alongside an active migration/sync ("target saturating, apply throttling"), squarely in sluice's wheelhouse; **(b) standalone monitor** — `sluice` as a general PS-metrics alerting daemon, broader than its migration core. Recommend starting with (a) (sync-scoped, low scope-creep) and the generic-webhook sink (covers Slack/email via the user's own relays), then evaluate (b) by demand.

**Gotchas.** (1) Scope discipline — sluice is a migration/sync tool; a *sync-scoped* alerter fits the tenets, a *general* monitoring daemon is adjacent and risks scope-creep (gate (b) on real demand). (2) Notification sinks are new outbound integration surface — keep them optional, credential-gated (Slack/SMTP creds distinct from DSNs), and failure-isolated (a dead Slack webhook must never stall or crash a sync). (3) Edge-trigger + cooldown so a flapping metric doesn't spam. (4) Engine-neutral core; the PS specifics stay in the item-32 provider, the alert/sink layer is generic. (5) Reuses item 35's rolling history for "rate of change" thresholds (e.g. storage climbing fast → pre-grow warning).

### 37. Proactive cold-copy back-off during a target storage-grow stall — coordinated pause-on-stall + (optional) Item-32-telemetry throttle — ✅ SHIPPED v0.99.100 (ADR-0110 `ir.GrowGate` coordinated grow-window pause; restore + native-sync wiring + quiet-cycle fix in later patches) — *operator-flagged 2026-06-22; the DEEPER fix behind the v0.99.92–v0.99.99 reactive storage-grow arc*

**SHIPPED (impl landed; pending the CI `-race` gate + release tag).** `ir.GrowGate` + `ir.GrowGateSetter` engine-neutral seam (`internal/ir/grow_gate.go`); `pipeline.growGate` single-owner coordinator (`internal/pipeline/grow_gate.go`) — one per cold-copy run, constructed unconditionally (zero-value-safe, no CLI flag), inert until tripped; hot-path `Await`/`Trip` in the MySQL write-lane reparent-retry and the pipeline source-read retry; telemetry-driven proactive trip + storage-recovery release wired through the cold-copy-phase storage-headroom watch (`startStorageHeadroomWatch` now gate-aware; apply-phase watch stays WARN-only). One deviation from the ADR sketch (race-safety): quiet-cycle window teardown instead of mid-window reopen/re-close — observably equivalent, single-owner / single-teardown. Concurrency chunk: the `-race` Integration job must pass before tag.

**Diagnostic verdict (2026-06-21, Track-D PS-320 v6–v9 — DONE).** The cause is being **mid-write into the volume during its grow/reparent serving-transition window**, NOT concurrency and NOT pathological data. Three runs on a *growing* 12 GB volume (v6/v7/v8) all froze at the SAME byte point (10.34 GB ≈ 86 % of the 12 GB volume = the auto-grow trigger threshold) and exhausted the retry budget; a v9 run on a volume that had ALREADY grown to 62 GB rode straight through that point with ZERO transient faces, copying the big `documents` MEDIUMTEXT table clean past its full row count. Ruled out: a 1-lane run stalled identically to a 16-lane run (concurrency irrelevant); `documents` copies fine on a pre-grown volume (data not pathological — it only looked like the culprit because it is the big table being hammered when the threshold trips). This REFRAMES the fix from "stop hammering to reduce contention" to "ride/avoid the resize window cleanly." **Design: ADR-0110** — one engine-neutral coordinated-pause primitive (`ir.GrowGate`) tripped from TWO sources sharing one mechanism: (1) signal-driven (baseline, no deps; first classified grow-transient on any lane quiesces all lanes; works for ANY auto-grow target incl. non-PlanetScale) + (2) telemetry-driven (precision; Item-32 storage-headroom sidecar trips the SAME gate proactively before transients start; PS-only, advisory). Operator confirmed BOTH (non-PS targets with similar auto-growth need the signal-driven floor regardless).

**Why.** v0.99.92–v0.99.99 made the cold-copy *ride through* a PlanetScale non-Metal storage auto-grow REACTIVELY: every transient face (reparent / source-read timeout / query-killer / disk-full errno-28 / 1114-table-full / 1205-lock-wait) is now retriable, and v0.99.99 widened the retry budget to ~15–20 min so a prolonged big-table grow step is ridden. That makes it WORK — but inefficiently: during the multi-minute stall, all ~16 cold-copy write lanes (W readers × D fan-out) independently hammer-retry the struggling target, which itself **prolongs** the stall (contention slows the grow + recovery) and breeds secondary errors (the 1205 lock-wait-timeouts were a *consequence* of the hammering). The live arc showed the copy spending 13–23 min thrashing through a grow that the target could have completed faster if left alone. The proactive fix treats the cause, not the symptom.

**What.** When a storage-grow stall is detected (a classified disk-full / `ResourceExhausted` / reparent transient on the write path), have the cold-copy **back off in a COORDINATED way** rather than per-lane independently: e.g. a shared pause barrier so all lanes quiesce together for a longer interval (let the volume grow without write pressure), then resume — instead of 16 lanes each retrying every ~30–60 s. Optionally (the elegant layer, building on the now-shipped **Item-32 Phase 2** provider): when target storage util / CPU saturation is observed approaching the grow boundary, **reduce write concurrency pre-emptively** (throttle the fan-out, or pause) BEFORE the cascade starts — anticipate the grow instead of reacting to its errors. Bounded + loud on genuine exhaustion, exactly as today; this only changes *how* the retry waits (coordinated + patient vs independent + hammering), not the correctness contract.

**Gotchas.** (1) Don't deadlock the fan-out — a coordinated pause must compose with the errgroup + the per-lane AIMD; a stalled lane holding the barrier must still honor ctx-cancel. (2) Keep it bounded + loud (a genuinely-dead target still surfaces; the pause just makes the wait calmer, not infinite). (3) The telemetry-throttle layer is OPTIONAL (needs the operator's metrics token) and ADVISORY — the reactive retry stays the authoritative floor, so a no-token run still rides through (just less efficiently). (4) Measure: the win is faster + calmer ride-through (less target thrashing, fewer secondary 1205s), not new correctness — validate against the same PS-320 storage-grow scenario the reactive arc used.

### 38. PG-TARGET cold-copy storage-grow resilience (the Postgres analog of items 30/33/37) — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.111** (chunked-COPY-with-grow-retry when a grow-gate is attached; PG `RowWriter` implements `ir.GrowGateSetter`; class-53 `53100`/`53000`/`53200` retriable arm shared with CDC apply; mirrors MySQL `flushWithReparentRetry`; value-fidelity-reviewed — byte-identical pin incl. `numeric[][]`/temporal/uuid/inet/bit codec families + retry-convergence + terminal-error-loud pins; v0.99.113 added the PG read-only-reparent face `pg_readonly`/XX000 retriable — the live re-validation rode 53100 disk-full but hit the read-only window, now also ridden) — *found live 2026-06-23 by the #94 MySQL→PS-160-Postgres test*

**Why.** The whole storage-grow resilience arc (items 30/33/37 — grow-gate, reparent/`not serving` retry, source-read resume, wall-clock retry bound) is **MySQL-target-only**: the retries are wired in the MySQL flush path (`flushWithReparentRetry`) and the grow-gate `Await` is on the MySQL write lane. A **Postgres target** cold-copy uses the `COPY`-protocol writer, which has NO equivalent. Live finding (#94): a MySQL→PS-160-Postgres cold-copy died ~4 GB in with `ERROR: could not extend file … No space left on device (SQLSTATE 53100)` — the PS non-Metal PG volume did not grow ahead of the streaming `COPY`, and the `COPY` aborted fatally instead of riding the grow. Loud-failure-safe (no data loss; `--reset-target-data` re-copies) but NOT resilient — the exact gap items 30/33/37 close for MySQL targets. (ADR-0108 already noted the PG `COPY`-path as a follow-up.)

**What.** Extend the cold-copy grow-window resilience to the PG `COPY` writer: classify the PG out-of-disk / serving-transition faces (`53100` could-not-extend-file, `57P01`/`57P03` admin-shutdown/cannot-connect-now during a reparent) as retriable, reconnect + resume the in-flight table/chunk (the keyset-chunked path is resumable; a single streaming `COPY` of one big table is the hard case — may need chunking the PG COPY too), and wire the `ir.GrowGate` `Await` into the PG write path so the signal-driven coordinated pause (item 37) covers PG targets. Bounded + loud on genuine exhaustion, same contract as MySQL.

**Gotchas.** (1) A single PG `COPY FROM STDIN` of one large table is one long operation — riding a mid-COPY grow may require splitting it (keyset chunks) so a retry has a resume point, or accepting table-granularity restart. (2) The grow-gate seam is engine-neutral already; the work is wiring `Await` into the PG writer + a PG-target error classifier (mirror `classifyApplierError`). (3) Validate against a fresh small-volume PS-160 PG so the grow re-triggers.

### 39. Extend items 35 + 36 (metrics history + threshold alerts) to the COLD-COPY phase — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.112** (recorder + alerter hoisted to a single per-attempt `startTelemetrySidecars` in runOnce right after the applier opens — covers cold-copy + CDC with one start; run-scoped ctx, no double-start, no cross-attempt leak; the applier is idle during cold-copy so reuse is safe) — *found 2026-06-23 during the #94 showcase*

**Why.** The item-35 rolling-history recorder and the item-36 threshold alerter are wired in `phaseStartApplySidecars` — the **CDC-apply phase**. So during a long **cold-copy** (the dominant phase of a big migration, and exactly when the target is under heavy write load and storage grows happen) neither records metrics history nor fires threshold alerts. The telemetry provider itself polls throughout (so the AIMD damp + the storage-headroom WARN + the grow-gate already cover cold-copy), but the new recorder/alerter sidecars miss it. The #94 showcase made this concrete: items 35/36 stayed dormant until the (small-subset) copy reached CDC.

**What.** Start the metrics-history recorder + the threshold alerter at cold-copy start too (or stream-construction), not only at apply-phase start. The alerter (item 36) needs only the provider + sinks (no target write) — trivial to start earlier. The recorder (item 35) needs a target connection for its metadata-table writes; during cold-copy the writer/RowWriter holds target connections but not a `ChangeApplier` (which carries the `TargetMetricsHistoryStore` seam), so either open a lightweight dedicated metadata connection for the recorder or surface the store off the cold-copy target pool. Keep both failure-isolated (a recorder/alerter hiccup must never affect the copy).

**Gotchas.** (1) One recorder per stream — don't double-start across the cold-copy→CDC transition (dedup or hand off). (2) The cold-copy phase is where storage-grow alerts matter MOST (pre-grow warning) — this is the highest-value window for item 36. (3) Engine-neutral; the metadata-store seam already exists.

### 40. Metrics-aware clamp on restore's auto `--bulk-parallelism` × `--table-parallelism` product (the PlanetScale-correct bound) — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.119 (ADR-0115)** — *operator-flagged 2026-06-23; follow-up to ADR-0112*

**SHIPPED:** extracted the `{1,2,4}` headroom-divisor thresholds from the apply-path `clampConcurrencyByHeadroom` into a shared `headroomDivisor(ctx, ir.TargetTelemetry)`; added optional `TargetTelemetry` to `Restore` (wired from the `restore` command's `--planetscale-*` flags); `resolveRestoreParallelism` now clamps the AUTO product by live CPU/mem headroom (cross-table axis absorbs first). Advisory/telemetry-gated/no-op when off; never raises; respects explicitly-pinned axes; floors at 1. Pinned by unit tests; `-race`-gated. Original write-up retained below for traceability.

**Why.** ADR-0112's within-table chunk parallelism is auto-on by default (`--bulk-parallelism 0` → `min(8, NumCPU)`, same `0→auto` pattern as `--apply-concurrency`/item 31). The `table × bulk` product is bounded at the connection-budget chokepoint — but **only for engines with a budget prober (Postgres)**. **MySQL/PlanetScale has no prober, so the product passes through UNCLAMPED.** And per the operator (2026-06-23): PlanetScale MySQL can carry many connections (VTGate fronts the pool — `conns=6/250` observed), so **connections are not the scarce resource; CPU is**, especially on small plans (PS-10 pinned at CPU 1.000 during the Track-C restore). So a connection-budget bound (item 41) is the *wrong* lever for PlanetScale — the right one is the **live CPU/mem telemetry** sluice already ships.

**What.** Route restore's auto-resolved `table × bulk` product through the **existing v0.99.106 `clampConcurrencyByHeadroom`** (quarter at ≥0.85 CPU/mem high-water, halve at ≥0.70) when a telemetry provider is wired — the same startup headroom clamp that already governs apply-lane auto:N. Restore-specific wiring only; the clamp logic + the telemetry seam are shipped. Startup-only (restore's partition is fixed once chosen; no mid-run re-partition). Degrades to today (unclamped auto) when no provider / no fresh sample — never raises an explicit operator value. Keeps restore correct either way (the reparent-retry already rides any over-aggression); this makes the auto-default *faster net* on small instances by not self-inflicting tx-killer/reparent churn.

**Gotchas.** (1) Restore has no AIMD (bulk INSERT, not CDC apply), so the clamp is the ONLY proactive throttle on the restore path — it's load-bearing for small targets, not just advisory. (2) Startup-only by design. (3) Telemetry-gated + failure-isolated (no provider ⇒ exactly today's behaviour).

### 41. MySQL `TargetConnectionBudgetProber` so restore/migrate parallelism is budget-bounded on self-hosted MySQL like Postgres — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.121 (ADR-0116)** — *the self-hosted-MySQL analog + the no-credential PlanetScale buffer-pool tier-proxy cap*

**SHIPPED:** MySQL `Engine` now implements `ir.TargetConnectionBudgetProber` (`internal/engines/mysql/connection_budget.go`): reads `@@max_connections`/`Threads_connected`/user-conn limit → CopyBudget, mirroring the PG path (loud refuse when 0 free, advisory degrade-and-proceed when managed quirks forbid the accounting queries). PLUS Part B — the no-credential CPU/tier proxy: `@@innodb_buffer_pool_size` bucketed (`<256 MB→2`, `<2 GB→4`, `<8 GB→6`, `≥8 GB→8`, live PS-10→PS-160 data) and folded as a MIN into the budget. The resolver picks it up structurally (no pipeline change). Complements ADR-0115's metrics clamp (telemetry = robust path; this = credential-free fallback + the genuine self-hosted-MySQL conn bound). Bucket boundaries pinned by a change-detector test; budget math + managed-permission-degrade unit-tested + container integration tests. Original write-up retained below.

**Why.** Postgres implements `ir.TargetConnectionBudgetProber`, so the copy-parallelism resolver bounds the `table × within` product to the target's real budget. MySQL implements no prober, so MySQL targets pass through unclamped. For a **self-hosted vanilla MySQL** with a genuine `max_connections` wall, that can over-subscribe the server. (For **PlanetScale** it's largely a no-op — VTGate's ceiling is big and CPU is the real limit, which item 40 handles.)

**What.** A MySQL `ProbeTargetConnectionBudget` reading `@@max_connections` + `Threads_connected` (in-use) + `@@max_user_connections` / `mysql.user.max_user_connections`, minus a reserve, returning the budget; the resolve path already calls the interface, so MySQL would just start participating and the product would clamp like Postgres. ~150–250 LOC + tests.

**PlanetScale tier-proxy sub-idea — VALIDATED LIVE 2026-06-23 (operator-flagged).** A no-credential, SQL-only alternative to the metrics-token path (item 40): infer the PlanetScale plan tier (≈ RAM ≈ vCPU) from a queryable server var and bucket a parallelism cap off it. Probed PS-10→PS-160 (throwaway DBs, deleted after) through VTGate — `@@innodb_buffer_pool_size` scales **monotonically and is NOT VTGate-masked**: PS-10 0.125 GB · PS-20 0.83 · PS-40 1.64 · PS-80 4.91 · PS-160 9.80 GB (PS-10's 128 MB == the MySQL stock default was a COINCIDENCE — the larger tiers prove it's a real per-tier value). `@@max_connections` (250/417/837/1671/3345) and `@@thread_cache_size` (10/12/16/24/41) corroborate. **Fixed across all tiers (useless as proxies):** `innodb_io_capacity` (2000), io threads (4r/8w), `table_open_cache` (4000), `innodb_buffer_pool_instances` (1), `innodb_redo_log_capacity` (100 MB). So a cap can bucket on `@@innodb_buffer_pool_size` (<256 MB → low … ≥6 GB → high) WITHOUT the metrics token — complements item 40 (the metrics-CPU runtime clamp is the robust always-correct path; this is the credential-free heuristic). NOTE the connection-budget reading ALSO tier-scales, so a plain MySQL prober isn't useless on PlanetScale — but it bounds connections (abundant: ≥250) not CPU (the real PS-10 limit), so the buffer-pool/tier signal is the better cap input.

**Gotchas.** (1) Per-user limits vs global — bound by the tighter. (2) A connection-budget prober alone bounds the wrong resource on PlanetScale (CPU is the limit, conns are abundant) — pair it with the buffer-pool tier-proxy cap above. (3) Demand-gated for the self-hosted-MySQL connection-wall case; the PlanetScale tier-proxy cap is the part worth building first (feeds item 40 with a no-credential signal).

### 42. PG-migrate overlapped copy+index path: ride a reparent inside the per-table index build (ADR-0114 residual) — **✅ SHIPPED v0.99.120**

**SHIPPED:** wrapped the overlap path's per-table `buildOneIndex` (`indexBuildWorkerTracked`) in `buildOneIndexWithReparentRetry` → the pure `retryIndexBuildWithReparent` policy, reusing the SAME envelope (`pgCopyReparent*Var` + `pgCopyReparentBackoff`) + `classifyApplierError` as the cold-copy chunk retry. On a classified transient it closes the dead pinned conn, backs off, re-acquires a FRESH conn (reparented primary), re-tunes, and replays the idempotent `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` instead of cancelling the errgroup; real DDL faults stay terminal; exhaustion is loud. Pure policy unit-pinned (rides-then-succeeds / terminal-no-retry / reacquire-transient-ridden / loud-exhaustion / ctx-cancel); `-race`-gated. Original write-up retained below.

**Why.** ADR-0114 (v0.99.118) wraps every post-copy DDL phase (`CreateIndexes`/`CreateConstraints`/`CreateViews`/`SyncIdentitySequences`) in an engine-general bounded reparent-retry, in BOTH `restore.go` and `migrate.go`. But the Postgres-migrate **overlapped copy+index** optimization (ADR-0077, `runOverlappedCopyAndIndexPhase` → `ir.IncrementalIndexBuilder.BuildTableIndexesFromChannel`) builds per-table indexes *interleaved with the copy*, INSIDE the engine method — so the pipeline-level wrap can't reach it. A storage-grow reparent landing on one of those interleaved index builds would still abort (the builder currently cancels the errgroup on the first build error). The live-failing path (Track-C restore) uses the now-wrapped `CreateIndexes`, not the overlap path, so this is a known residual, not a regression.

**What.** Push a classify-and-retry INTO the engine's per-table index build: on a classified `ir.RetriableError` (the same `classifyApplierError` verdict ADR-0114's `ir.TransientClassifier` exposes), back off + re-run that table's `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` (idempotent) instead of cancelling the group. Mirror the ADR-0114 envelope (~30-min wall-clock, loud on exhaustion). Pin with a fake builder that fails one table's build with a transient then succeeds.

**Gotchas.** (1) The build runs concurrently with the copy pool, so the retry must not wedge the `completedTables` channel drain. (2) Only the index BUILD is retriable; a real DDL fault stays terminal (loud). (3) Demand-gated — only the PG-migrate (not restore, not MySQL) overlap path is exposed, and only on a target that reparents mid-index-build.

### 43. LATENT cross-engine SILENT-LOSS: two source tables sharing a long/colliding index name collapse to one on the PG target (the `pgIndexName` verbatim escape hatch) — ✅ SHIPPED v0.99.125 (loud refusal at the emit chokepoint)

**Why (flagged by the Bug #114 RCA, 2026-06-24 — NOT triggered by that schema, but a real silent-loss class).** PG index names are schema-GLOBAL (unique in `pg_class` per namespace); MySQL index names are per-TABLE. sluice's `pgIndexName` (`internal/engines/postgres/ddl_emit.go:~800`) disambiguates by prefixing the table name (`idx_x` on `inventory` → `inventory_idx_x`), which is why Bug #114 was NOT an index-name collision. **But** `pgIndexName` intentionally returns the source name **verbatim** when prefixing would overflow PG's 63-char identifier limit, and on convention-prefix matches. So if two source tables genuinely share a >63-char index name (or a colliding convention shape), they emit the SAME PG relation name → the serial index path's `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` **silently skips the second table's index** (a missing-index silent-correctness loss — wrong-but-plausible, exit 0). The concurrent pool would instead loudly `23505` (now ridden by the #114 catalog-race retry — which would mask it further on the serial path). The escape hatch is documented in-code as a deliberate trade.

**What.** When two distinct source indexes would emit the same PG name, REFUSE LOUDLY (naming both source `table.index` + the collision) rather than silently coalescing — or hash-suffix to a guaranteed-unique ≤63-char name. Value-fidelity lens: a missing index is silent. Pin the class: long-name overflow + convention-prefix collision across ≥2 tables, asserting a loud refusal (or distinct emitted names), not a silent skip.

**Gotchas.** (1) Must compare EMITTED PG names, not source names. (2) The 63-char truncation is the trigger — test at the boundary. (3) Demand-gated (requires two tables sharing a long/colliding index name); LOW likelihood but a genuine silent-loss class, so worth a loud-refusal pin.

**Shipped (v0.99.125).** Loud refusal, not hash-suffix (per "contain Postgres complexity, surface explicitly" — auto-rename silently transforms the operator's schema). A byte-length preflight `validatePGIndexName` (`internal/engines/postgres/ddl_emit.go`) is called at the index-emit chokepoint `emitCreateIndex` (covers the live serial/concurrent/overlap `buildOneIndex` paths and the dry-run `PreviewDDL`) and at the inline unique-key constraint promoted in `emitTableDef`. The check is BYTE-based (matches PG's NAMEDATALEN), refusing any EFFECTIVE name >63 bytes with an error naming the index, byte length, table, and remedy. The >63-byte refusal is sufficient for the same-prefix-collision class: two DISTINCT ≤63-byte names can only share a 63-byte truncation prefix if they are byte-identical (= the same catalog ident, of which the IR carries one). Pinned: `TestEmitCreateIndex_NameLengthRefusal` (63 accepted / 64 refused-with-name / multibyte rune≤63-byte>63 refused / two-names-after-byte-63 both refused) + `TestValidatePGIndexName_Boundary`. The v0.49.0 GitHub-#26 generative-overflow behaviour (prepend-then-verbatim for ≤63-byte source names) is unchanged.

---

### 44. CDC schema-forward onto a LARGE, already-serving target: bound lock-taking DDL + (optionally) rewrite dangerous ALTERs into the safe multi-step form — *flagged 2026-06-25 (operator "dangerous migrations" research item); DEMAND-GATED, LOW priority*

**Why.** sluice's dominant model applies DDL to a target it is *building* (empty → bulk-load → indexes → constraints), so the classic "dangerous migration" hazards (a lock-taking / table-rewriting ALTER that blocks production traffic — `ALTER COLUMN TYPE`, validating `ADD FK`/`CHECK`, `SET NOT NULL`, non-`CONCURRENTLY` `CREATE INDEX`) are structurally absent: the target isn't serving, and plain `CREATE INDEX` is correctly *faster* there than `CONCURRENTLY`. The ONE real exposure is the **CDC schema-forward path** (`internal/pipeline/schema_forward_intercept.go`): when the SOURCE runs such an ALTER mid-sync, sluice forwards that DDL onto a target that may already be large and read-served (pre-cutover) — there a forwarded `ALTER COLUMN TYPE` (rewrite under `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE`) or validating FK can lock/rewrite a big live target table, and a lock-taker can queue behind a long read and block everything behind it.

**What.** Two independent, additive mitigations: **(1)** set a bounded `lock_timeout` (and consider `statement_timeout`) on the target DDL session for the schema-forward path so a forwarded lock-taker fails fast + retries (via the existing transient-retry classifier) instead of blocking the target indefinitely — a small, contained change. **(2)** OPTIONALLY rewrite a forwarded dangerous source ALTER into the canon safe multi-step form on the target (`ADD FK … NOT VALID` then `VALIDATE`; `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY`; `ADD CHECK … NOT VALID`/`VALIDATE` for `SET NOT NULL`) — sluice already does the orphan-FK `NOT VALID` retry (`schema_writer.go:717-785`), so this generalizes an existing pattern. Larger surface; do only if a real large-live-target schema-forward use case lands.

**Gotchas.** (1) Does NOT affect the build-fresh-target flow (no behavior change there). (2) `lock_timeout` must NOT bleed into the bulk-copy/connection-budget sessions — scope it to the DDL-apply path only. (3) The safe-DDL rewrite is engine-specific (PG `CONCURRENTLY`/`NOT VALID`; MySQL online-DDL `ALGORITHM=INPLACE/INSTANT, LOCK=NONE`) and must stay IR-mediated, not regex-over-DDL. (4) Demand-gated: no current use case exercises schema-forward onto a large serving target; the build-fresh-target path is the overwhelming majority.

---

> **Items 45–47 form one coherent "sync control plane" direction** (operator-flagged 2026-06-25): turn sluice from a tool you run per-migration into a long-running sync fabric you *operate* — many supervised syncs (47), any of them optionally lag-delayed for DR (46), all of them health-alerted against their source (45). Queued as worthwhile next work (not demand-gated); suggested order is 45 → 46 → 47 (cheapest/broadest first, unifying layer last). Each builds directly on shipped foundations (bounded streaming, the notify layer, per-stream metrics).

### 45. Source-vs-target lag alerting: an engine-neutral "seconds behind source" metric + threshold alert — *SHIPPED (v0.99.129): `sluice_sync_lag_seconds` + `--notify-sync-lag-seconds`, ungated from PS telemetry*

**Why.** The notification machinery is already shipped (item 36 / ADR-0107: webhook + Slack sinks, an edge-triggered threshold alerter with per-rule cooldown + hysteresis, and a `--notify-lag-seconds` rule). But that lag rule reads the **target's control-plane replica lag from PlanetScale telemetry** (`sluice_target_replica_lag_seconds`, PS-gated) — there is no engine-agnostic alert on sluice's **own** sync lag: how far the applied target position trails the source's latest commit. That "is my target keeping up with my source" signal is exactly what an operator wants to be paged on, and it should work for MySQL and Postgres alike, with no PlanetScale dependency.

**What.** Surface a first-class engine-neutral sync-lag metric — source latest-commit timestamp minus the applied-position commit timestamp ("seconds behind source") — exported as `sluice_sync_lag_seconds` alongside the existing gauges, and wire it into the existing threshold-alerter UNGATED from PS telemetry. The sink / cooldown / hysteresis / Slack plumbing already exists; this is "add one metric + one rule," so the surface is small.

**Gotchas.** (1) Time-based lag needs source commit timestamps — CDC changes already carry them (binlog/GTID event time, VStream event time). (2) Define lag HONESTLY when idle: no new source commits ⇒ lag is 0/caught-up, not a growing number (a common false-alarm class). (3) Multi-shard VStream: report max-across-shards (the slowest shard is the lag). (4) Keep it distinct from the existing PS control-plane `sluice_target_replica_lag_seconds` (different metric name, different meaning — apply lag vs target-internal replica lag). (5) Must subtract item 46's intentional delay if both are engaged (don't page on a deliberately-delayed replica).

**Impl notes (as shipped).** The IR `Change` interface gained `SourceCommitTime()` (a new `CommitTime` field on every variant); each CDC reader populates it (native-MySQL binlog `hdr.Timestamp`; VStream `VEvent.Timestamp`; PG pgoutput Begin/Commit `CommitTime`; postgres-trigger `committed_at`). The lag is tracked in-process by `internal/pipeline.syncLagTracker` (lock-free atomics) fed by a streamer-side change-stream interceptor (`observeSyncLagChanges`), exposed via the metrics server (`AttachSyncLagSource` → `sluice_sync_lag_seconds`) and the new ungated alerter (`startSyncLagNotifier`, sharing the ADR-0107 edge/cooldown/hysteresis decision via the extracted `evalThresholdAlert`). No new ADR — this is an ADR-0107 amendment (a second, telemetry-independent rule reusing the same notify layer). Deviations from the spec's gotchas: **(2) idle honesty** is implemented by FREEZING the lag at apply time (it never ages between changes) plus a `syncLagCaughtUpAfter` (30s) window that retires a stale reading to 0 — chosen over a true source-head-position signal (which the IR does not expose engine-neutrally); the documented trade-off is that a behind-AND-wedged stream (nothing flowing) also reads 0, which is the complementary job of `sluice_seconds_since_last_apply` (which ages). **(3) multi-shard "max-across-shards"** is approximated, not exact: IR changes carry no shard identity, so the tracker reports the lag of the most-recently-applied change over the single merged VStream channel; because a lagging shard continuously delivers older-commit events into that channel, the reading surfaces the slowest active shard's lag as those events flow (operators wanting a hard max should `max_over_time(sluice_sync_lag_seconds[…])` in Prometheus). **(5) item 46 apply-delay subtraction** is a no-op today — item 46 (delayed replica) is not yet shipped; when it lands, the delay must be subtracted at the tracker's `observe` so a deliberately-delayed replica doesn't page.

---

### 46. Delayed replica: keep the target a configurable interval behind the source — *SHIPPED (ADR-0121); see impl notes below*

**Impl notes (SHIPPED).** `--apply-delay DURATION` on `sync start` (+ `Streamer.ApplyDelay`), realized as a single pass-through interceptor `delayChanges` (`internal/pipeline/apply_delay.go`) wired into `phaseWireInterceptChain` BEFORE the item-45 sync-lag observer. It holds each change until `SourceCommitTime() + delay ≤ now` (using the item-45 `ir.Change.SourceCommitTime()` the readers already populate), then forwards it; zero-commit-time changes (SchemaSnapshot, sources that supply none) and already-past releases forward immediately. **Design = the hold-at-apply backpressure gate, NOT an in-heap buffer** (the roadmap's preference): the gate holds at most ONE change and blocks on the sleep before reading the next, so the source read backpressures behind it — bounded memory, trivial resume. (1) **Resume/exactly-once** is satisfied by construction: the gate sits UPSTREAM of the applier, which is the only thing that advances the durable position (ADR-0007, position written in the same tx as the data), so a held-but-unapplied change never advances the position; on ctx-cancel mid-hold the gate drops the held change WITHOUT forwarding it, and resume re-reads it (idempotent replay, ADR-0010) — the delay window is never the sole home of an un-applied change. **PG slot-ack prerequisite (discovered + fixed here, ADR-0121 §2a):** the sluice-level invariant alone is insufficient on Postgres because the replication slot's `confirmed_flush_lsn` is a separate ack. Building this surfaced a pre-existing latent bug — the PG reader's `AttachLSNTracker(*lsnTracker)` did NOT satisfy the streamer's engine-neutral `AttachLSNTracker(any)` wiring interface, so the ADR-0020 slot-ack-after-apply tracker was NEVER attached on the streamer path and the keepalive acked the DECODED LSN. Masked by lockstep apply for every prior sync; `--apply-delay` (reader runs far ahead) turned it into active silent loss (ground-truthed: confirmed_flush ran ~5 rows past applied → warm resume lost rows). Fixed: reader takes `any` + internal assert (the documented contract) + a compile-time contract pin; now confirmed_flush trails applied for ALL PG syncs (strictly safer). Concurrency-adjacent → CI `-race`. (2) **Bounded memory** via backpressure (no spill needed); the documented tradeoff (ADR-0121 §3) is that backpressuring the reader past the source's replication idle timeout (PG `wal_sender_timeout`, MySQL `net_write_timeout`/`slave_net_timeout`) can reap the connection → reconnect-and-replay (correct, churny) — raise those server timeouts for large delays. (3) **Lag alerting:** the configured delay is subtracted in `syncLagTracker.observe` (`newSyncLagTracker(applyDelay)`) so a delayed replica reads ~0 lag, not `delay` seconds. **Transaction atomicity:** every row event in a source tx carries that tx's commit timestamp, so the whole tx releases at one instant — never split across the delay (ADR-0121 §4). Off by default (0 = byte-identical apply path, zero-value-safe). Concurrency-adjacent (extra goroutine + wall-clock timing) → the CI `-race` integration job must pass before any tag. Tests: unit (`apply_delay_test.go`: future-held / past-immediate / zero-commit-immediate / whole-tx-releases-together / ctx-cancel-drops-held-change resume-safety pin / source-close drain) + the lag-subtraction pin (`sync_lag_test.go`) + a PG→PG integration test (`apply_delay_integration_test.go`: cold-copy unaffected, CDC held then released, and the load-bearing crash-mid-delay-window → restart → exactly-11-rows resume pin). Docs: ADR-0121, this entry, CHANGELOG.

**Why.** The "oops window" disaster-recovery pattern (MySQL's `MASTER_DELAY` analog): a deliberately N-minutes-behind target gives an operator time to **stop sluice before an accidental `DROP TABLE` / bad migration / runaway `DELETE` on the source replicates**, then recover from the still-intact target. It's cheap, comprehensible point-in-time protection that complements the logical-backup track. Nothing like it exists today — CDC applies as fast as it can.

**What.** An `--apply-delay DURATION` knob: hold each CDC change until `commit_ts + delay ≤ now` before applying it. Engine-neutral, lives in the streamer apply loop; the cold-copy phase is unaffected (only steady-state CDC delays).

**Gotchas.** (1) Resume / exactly-once: the delay buffer must NEVER be the only home of un-applied changes — resume restarts from the last **applied** position and re-reads the delayed window (the position model already supports resuming from an older point); a process crash must not lose the buffered-but-unapplied tail. (2) Bounded memory: the buffer is `≤ delay × write-rate`, which can be large, so it must backpressure / spill rather than balloon (the bounded-streaming discipline the memory-soak work validated). (3) Lag alerting (item 45) must treat the configured delay as expected, not as falling behind.

---

### 47. Sync command center: supervise many syncs from one sluice instance + aggregated status/dashboard — *MINIMAL-FIRST SHIPPED (ADR-0122); web dashboard SHIPPED (ADR-0124); terminal TUI SHIPPED (ADR-0125); per-sync PlanetScale telemetry SHIPPED this release (ADR-0126)*

**Impl notes (SHIPPED, minimal-first).** `sluice sync run --config syncs.yaml` supervises N independent `pipeline.Streamer` syncs in ONE process via the engine-neutral `pipeline.Supervisor` (`internal/pipeline/supervisor.go`): each sync runs in its own goroutine, FAILURE-ISOLATED (a panic is `recover`ed into an error so it can never crash the process / take down peers — the load-bearing property), restarted on bounded exponential backoff (default 1s→30s, `restart.max-consecutive-failures` cap, 0 = unbounded; the consecutive counter resets after a healthy run per ADR-0038), with a clean ctx-cancel draining all. The fleet config is a typed koanf YAML (`cmd/sluice/sync_run.go`, `SyncSpec` = a curated subset of the `sync start` flag surface, kebab-case keys); the spec→Streamer build reuses the exact `sync start` helpers. Two data-corruption classes are refused LOUDLY at config-load: duplicate resolved Postgres replication-slot names across PG syncs (gotcha 3), and duplicate stream-ids (clobbered position row); a shared target server WARNs about the shared connection budget (gotcha 2). `sluice sync status --all --config syncs.yaml` (`cmd/sluice/sync_status_all.go`) rolls the existing per-stream status up across every configured target (deduped; an unreachable target reported-and-skipped) through the EXISTING `renderStatus`. Failure isolation (gotcha 1) is pinned by a deterministic unit test with stubbed runners + a PG→PG integration test. **Config hot-reload (gotcha 4) is now SHIPPED (ADR-0122 §7):** a `SIGHUP` on a running `sync run` re-reads + re-validates the config and `pipeline.Supervisor.Reconcile`s the live fleet (add / remove / restart by stream-id, fingerprint-diffed) without a process restart; a bad reload (parse / validation / slot or stream-id collision) is refused loudly and the live fleet keeps running on the old config unchanged — the load-bearing reject-and-keep-running property. POSIX-only (the SIGHUP trigger is build-tagged `!windows`; the portable `Reconcile` is unit-tested cross-platform + a PG→PG reconcile-restart integration pin shows clean slot release/reacquire). **Per-sync PlanetScale telemetry is now SHIPPED (ADR-0126):** `SyncSpec` gains the `planetscale-*` + `suppress-target-metrics-history` + PS-gated `notify-*` keys (env-first token via `PLANETSCALE_METRICS_TOKEN_ID` / `PLANETSCALE_METRICS_TOKEN`); a sync that sets `planetscale-org` without a resolvable token is refused at config-load (named by stream-id), and `buildSupervisedFleet` builds + attaches one independent `ir.TargetTelemetry` provider per telemetry-enabled sync (each watching its own PlanetScale target — headroom clamp + `sluice_target_*{stream_id}` metrics + PS-gated alerts + `diagnose`), closed on fleet exit; the `--dry-run` plan shows `telemetry=org/db@branch` per sync without the token. Additive plumbing — no value-path or global-state change. Still deferred: per-sync MySQL process-globals (`--mysql-sql-mode` / `--zero-date` / VStream tuning are set once per process). **The web dashboard layer is now SHIPPED (ADR-0124):** opt-in `sluice sync run --dashboard-listen ADDR` serves a read-only, auto-refreshing HTML fleet view (`GET /`) plus a stable JSON API (`GET /api/fleet`) and a `GET /healthz` probe from a tiny stdlib server (`internal/pipeline/dashboard.go` + the embedded `dashboard.html`), derived PURELY from `Supervisor.Snapshot()` — no data path, no mutation, no controls, failure-isolated like the `/metrics` server, zero-value-safe (empty addr ⇒ off; never under `--dry-run`), no-auth (bind to localhost / a trusted network). Concurrency chunk: the CI `-race` integration job gates it. **The terminal TUI layer is now SHIPPED (ADR-0125):** `sluice sync tui --connect ADDR` is a full-screen bubbletea/lipgloss client that polls the same `/api/fleet` JSON on a ticker (`--refresh`, default 2s) and renders the live fleet — a color-coded table with ↑/↓ row selection, an `enter` detail pane (full un-truncated last error + timestamps), and an unreachable banner that keeps the last-known fleet on screen. Read-only and decoupled from the supervisor (it's an HTTP client of the dashboard API, the k9s/lazygit shape), so it also works against a remote fleet over an SSH tunnel; the bubbletea model lives in the testable `internal/fleettui` package (pure `Update`, deterministic `View`) with the bubbletea/lipgloss dependency confined to that package + `cmd/sluice/sync_tui.go`. Per-sync lag/throughput in either surface (scraping the per-sync `/metrics` or widening the runner snapshot) remains a documented follow-up.

**Why.** Shifts sluice from "a tool you run per-migration" to "a sync fabric you operate." Today each `sluice sync start` is one source→target stream in its own process; the observability primitives already exist (per-stream `sync status` / `sync-health` / `/metrics`, the standalone `metrics-watch` daemon, and `sync status` already renders in terms of "N streams"), but there is no layer to **drive and aggregate many syncs at once** — which is what an operator keeping several ongoing cross-database syncs alive actually wants.

**What.** Stage it. Minimal first: `sluice sync run --config syncs.yaml` that supervises N streams in ONE process (each its own stream-id, with independent failure isolation + restart) plus `sync status --all` that rolls up the existing per-stream status/metrics into a fleet view. A TUI / web dashboard is a later layer over the already-exported metrics, not v1.

**Gotchas.** (1) Failure isolation is the load-bearing part — one sync dying must NOT take down the others (independent ctx / retry / restart per stream). (2) Shared connection-budget accounting when several syncs target one server. (3) Distinct replication-slot names per Postgres sync (the `--slot-name` convention already supports this; the supervisor must enforce uniqueness). (4) Config hot-reload was deferred from v1 — now SHIPPED as the item-47 follow-up (ADR-0122 §7, SIGHUP). Composes with item 45 (per-sync lag alerts roll up to the fleet view) and item 46 (any supervised sync can be delayed).

---

### 48. Email / SMTP notification sink — complete the notify-sink set — *SHIPPED (ADR-0107 amendment); see impl notes below*

**Impl notes (SHIPPED).** Built on `github.com/wneessen/go-mail` (the researched pick — context-aware, MIT, deps = only `golang.org/x/text`, lean as advertised). `internal/notify/smtp.go` adds `SMTPNotifier` + `SMTPConfig` implementing the existing `notify.Notifier` interface with the same advisory + failure-isolated semantics (a dead relay → returned error the `MultiNotifier` joins and the alerter logs-and-swallows). `internal/notify/email_template.go` renders a clean subject (`[sluice] <metric> threshold alert: <stream>`), a level-coloured HTML card, and a plaintext alternative carrying the same facts. Wired into the SHARED `buildMetricsNotifierFrom` so BOTH the sync-path alerter and the `metrics-watch` daemon deliver every alert (the ADR-0107 rules + item 45's sync-lag rule) by email. Flags on `sync start` + `metrics-watch`: `--notify-smtp-host/-port/-from/-to` (repeatable `-to`), `--notify-smtp-tls` (starttls|implicit|none), `--notify-smtp-auth` (none|plain|login) + `--notify-smtp-username`; password via `SLUICE_NOTIFY_SMTP_PASSWORD` env ONLY (no CLI flag value path). Opt-in, zero-value-off (inert unless host set); a half-configured sink is refused loudly at startup naming the missing flag (`SMTPConfig.Validate`). Tests: unit (config/validation matrix, HTML+text rendering, HTML auto-escape, zero-value-off, dead-relay failure isolation, TLS×auth client-build matrix) + a hermetic Mailpit testcontainer integration test (`smtp_integration_test.go`) asserting captured subject/recipient/both bodies. `internal/notify` added to the CI integration shard `engines-postgres-and-rest` + `scripts/check-shard-coverage.sh`. Rendered sample emails committed at `docs/operator/email-samples/{storage-util,sync-lag,cpu-util}.{html,txt}` (generator: `TestRenderEmailSamples`, gated on `SLUICE_WRITE_EMAIL_SAMPLES`). Closes the notify-sink set.

**Why.** Item 36 / ADR-0107 shipped the generic-webhook + Slack sinks and deferred email ("the generic webhook + Slack cover email via the user's own relay"). But email/SMTP is still the most universal alert channel, and a SINGLE SMTP sink covers every transactional provider (SendGrid is `smtp.sendgrid.net` user `apikey` / pass = API key; Mailgun, SES, Postmark all the same) **and** self-hosted/corporate relays — so one sink delivers broad coverage without N provider-specific HTTP integrations (the already-shipped generic webhook covers anyone who'd rather hit a provider's HTTP API directly).

**Why.** Item 36 / ADR-0107 shipped the generic-webhook + Slack sinks and deferred email ("the generic webhook + Slack cover email via the user's own relay"). But email/SMTP is still the most universal alert channel, and a SINGLE SMTP sink covers every transactional provider (SendGrid is `smtp.sendgrid.net` user `apikey` / pass = API key; Mailgun, SES, Postmark all the same) **and** self-hosted/corporate relays — so one sink delivers broad coverage without N provider-specific HTTP integrations (the already-shipped generic webhook covers anyone who'd rather hit a provider's HTTP API directly).

**What.** An SMTP sink implementing the existing notify sink interface, with the SAME semantics as the webhook/Slack sinks: opt-in, credential-via-env (`SLUICE_NOTIFY_SMTP_PASSWORD`, never the command line), and **advisory + failure-isolated** (a dead relay is logged-and-swallowed, never affects the sync). Config: `--notify-smtp-host` / `-port` / `-from` / `-to` + STARTTLS-vs-implicit-TLS + PLAIN/LOGIN auth + a from/to/subject template. Wire it into the SAME threshold-alerter (and item 45's source-lag rule) so it fires the identical edge-trigger + cooldown + hysteresis alerts the other sinks do.

**Library (researched 2026-06-25).** Lean toward **`github.com/wneessen/go-mail`** — the modern de-facto Go email library: actively maintained (v0.7.x, 2026), **context-aware** (fits sluice's ctx-heavy apply loop + timeout/cancellation), **minimal dependency footprint** (Go stdlib + golang.org/x, explicitly no 3rd-party deps), **MIT** (Apache-2.0-compatible), full STARTTLS + implicit-TLS + PLAIN/LOGIN/CRAM-MD5/XOAUTH2. Alternatives weighed: stdlib `net/smtp` (frozen + minimal — PLAIN-only, no context, known footguns; viable only for the barest v1) and `xhit/go-simple-mail` (MIT, low-dep, but **no context support** and no release since 2023). Final pick at implementation time, but go-mail is the front-runner.

**Gotchas.** Fully testable WITHOUT a real provider — a fake SMTP server (mailpit / MailHog / smtp4dev) in a testcontainer captures the message; the test asserts subject/body/recipient (hermetic, no secrets in CI), mirroring the webhook sink's local-HTTP-capture test. Keep the credential env-only. This closes the notify-sink set — the SMTP/email sink was the last channel demand-deferred at item 36.

### 49. SQLite / Cloudflare D1 migrate source engine (operator-flagged 2026-06-26) — *PROTOTYPE + date/bool policy + `.sql`-dump ingest + `_cf_*` auto-skip + native D1 query-API reader + schema-feature carry (generated/CHECK/partial+expression indexes) + within-table chunking (binary `.db`) + trigger-based CDC source Phase 1 (`sqlite-trigger`) AND Phase 2 (`d1-trigger`, D1-over-HTTP) SHIPPED + change-log retention Phase A (`sluice trigger prune`, Bug 165) SHIPPED + Phase B automatic in-stream pruning (`--auto-prune-change-log`) SHIPPED v0.99.174, hardened 2026-07-03 with batched keyset DELETEs + per-tick time budget + D1 poll-batch clamp (audit P-1/P-3) + SQLite→canonical (PG/MySQL) expression translator SHIPPED (ADR-0128, ADR-0129, ADR-0130, ADR-0132, ADR-0133, ADR-0135, ADR-0136, ADR-0137); trigger-CDC Phase 3 (schema-change forwarding / capture-payload trimming / replica-aware poll) + strftime/epoch expression translation + per-column encoding map DEFERRED*

**Trigger-based CDC source — Phase 1 SHIPPED (#5 of the SQLite queue, ADR-0135).** A LOCAL SQLite file now streams continuous logical CDC to a Postgres/MySQL target via the new `sqlite-trigger` engine (`internal/engines/sqlite-trigger`), the proven `pgtrigger` model (ADR-0066): `sluice trigger setup --source-driver sqlite-trigger --dsn ./app.db --tables=…` installs a `sluice_change_log` table + `sluice_change_log_meta` + per-table AFTER INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE capture triggers, and `sluice sync start --source-driver sqlite-trigger` does a cold-start snapshot (delegating to the validated `sqlite` reader — chunking + ADR-0129 date/bool) handed off gap-free to a polling CDC reader (monotonic-id watermark, exactly-once resume). The engine composes `sqlite` by delegation (CDC source only; write/target Open* not-implemented) and self-registers `sqlite-trigger`. **The faithful-capture crux (the load-bearing decision):** the trigger does NOT `json_object()` the raw columns (which rounds integers > 2^53 to a JSON double and can't represent a BLOB) — it captures each column as a `(typeof, text/hex)` pair using the SAME shared expression as the `d1` reader (`sqlite.CapturedValueExpr`/`CapturedTypeofExpr`), and the reader reconstructs the exact `int64`/`float64`/text/`[]byte` through the SAME `decodeCell` (`sqlite.CapturedCellDecoder`) — one decode implementation, big-int/BLOB EXACT (integration-proven into PG AND MySQL, plus a hard-stop/warm-resume exactly-once leg). SQLite's single-writer commit-ordered AUTOINCREMENT id means NO safety-lag predicate and a simple `MAX(id)`-before-snapshot anchor (gap-free; over-replay idempotent) — the load-bearing simplification over pgtrigger's bigserial contiguous-prefix anchor. A PK-less table is refused loudly at setup.

**Trigger-based CDC source — Phase 2 SHIPPED (#5 of the SQLite queue, ADR-0136): the `d1-trigger` engine streams a LIVE Cloudflare D1 database over the HTTP query API.** Phase 2 is transport substitution, not new CDC logic: `sluice trigger setup --source-driver d1-trigger --dsn d1://<account>/<db> --tables=…` installs the SAME change-log/meta/fingerprint schema + per-table capture triggers as Phase 1, and `sluice sync start --source-driver d1-trigger` does a cold-start snapshot (delegating to the lossless `d1` reader, ADR-0132) handed off gap-free to the polling CDC reader. The Phase-1 `sqlite-trigger` logic was refactored to run against a small executor seam (`internal/engines/sqlite-trigger/cdc_executor.go`) with TWO impls — the existing local `*sql.DB` path (kept byte-identical; the v0.99.148 tests re-pass unchanged) and a new D1 path backed by the `d1` reader's `/query` transport (`sqlite.D1Conn`) — and the `d1-trigger` engine (`internal/engines/d1-trigger`) composes the `d1` engine by delegation for cold-start and the shared D1 entry points for setup/CDC. Faithful capture/decode is byte-identical to Phase 1 (the same `(typeof, text/hex)` seam + `decodeCell`); big-int/BLOB EXACT over HTTP. The poll binds the watermark as a STRING param (no JS-rounding of a > 2^53 bound) and uses D1's DEFAULT primary (strongly-consistent) query path — NOT Sessions/read-replica routing, because commit-order = id-order holds at the write-serialised primary but can wobble against a lagging replica (ADR-0136 §4). Token env-only (`CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`), account from the DSN or `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID`; missing token/account refused loudly at open. Pinned by httptest unit tests (setup DDL bodies, poll SELECT + string watermark, big-int/real/blob/NULL fidelity over HTTP, watermark resume, schema-drift refusal, token/account refusals); live-D1 validation runs separately. **Phase 3 DEFERRED:** capture-payload trimming (to cut D1 write amplification), schema-change forwarding (SQLite/D1 have no DDL triggers → a source `ALTER TABLE` requires re-setup), and a replica-aware poll mode (Sessions API + safety-lag). (Change-log retention is no longer here — see the retention note below.)

**Change-log retention — Phase A SHIPPED (Bug 165, ADR-0137): `sluice trigger prune`.** The three trigger-CDC engines (`sqlite-trigger`, `d1-trigger`, `pgtrigger`) capture every source change into `sluice_change_log` and never reaped consumed rows, so the change-log grows unbounded for the life of a continuous sync (a Bug-165 run bloated a 476 MB source `.db` to 1.06 GB / 732k change rows in 3 minutes; on D1 it is also billable rows-written/storage). The new operator-run, cron-able `sluice trigger prune --source-driver … --source … --target-driver … --target … --stream-id …` reaps rows the TARGET has already durably applied: it reads the durably-persisted CDC position from the target (the same cdc-state row the applier writes / `sync status` reads — reusing `ChangeApplier.ReadPosition`), extracts the applied `last_id` via the engine's position codec (the new `AppliedLastID` helper on each trigger package), and `DELETE`s `sluice_change_log` rows with `id <= (applied_last_id - --keep)` on the SOURCE — engine-dispatched (SQLite over the file `*sql.DB`, D1 over the `/query` HTTP API, PG over SQL; the SQLite/D1 path reuses the ADR-0136 executor seam, extended with `pruneChangeLog`/`vacuum`/`changeLogStats`). **The correctness crux (silent-loss avoidance):** the prune bound is the TARGET's durable frontier, NEVER the source reader's read-cursor (which runs ahead) or the source `MAX(id)` — pruning there would delete not-yet-applied rows → warm-resume reads `id > durable_watermark`, finds them gone → silent permanent loss. The command REFUSES LOUDLY (exit non-zero) if it cannot read the target's durable position; there is no prune-blind mode. Two further foot-guns are loud (the loud-failure tenet): a `--stream-id` whose position is a FOREIGN (non-trigger-CDC) token — pgoutput/GTID/broker — that would otherwise decode to `last_id=0` is refused (`AppliedLastID` requires the `last_id` key via a `*int64` presence check); and a `--source`/`--stream-id` mis-pairing is cross-checked against the stream's recorded source fingerprint (ADR-0031, `pipeline.FingerprintSourceDSN`) and refused on mismatch for PG sources — SQLite-file/D1 sources carry no host:port:db fingerprint, so the cross-check can't run there (prints a `note:`; the operator doc warns to pass the exact pair; a file/D1 fingerprint is a tracked Phase-A.1 follow-up). Idempotent + safe to run while a sync is live (it only removes rows the target already durably applied). `--keep N` (default 1000) margin; `--vacuum` (SQLite/D1 only, off by default) reclaims file space; PG relies on autovacuum; `--dry-run` previews the bound. Pinned by unit tests (prune-bound math; the `id <= cut` boundary over a real temp SQLite file; refuse-on-garbled/foreign-token) + cross-engine integration (`sqlite-trigger` AND `pgtrigger` → PG: rows ≤ cut reaped, durable position unchanged, warm-resume after prune still exactly-once, plus a `--keep 0` leg deleting `id == applied_last_id` exactly). Operator doc: `docs/operator/trigger-changelog-retention.md`. **Phase B DEFERRED:** automatic in-stream pruning (the streamer prunes on a durable-checkpoint cadence so operators don't schedule anything) — needs the applier's durable-checkpoint signal threaded back to a source-side prune + cadence tuning (ADR-0137 §Decision 2).

**Within-table parallel-copy chunking — SHIPPED (#3 of the SQLite queue, ADR-0128).** The `sqlite` file `RowReader` now implements the optional parallel-bulk-copy surfaces (`BatchedRowReader`/`BoundedBatchedRowReader`, `RangeBoundsQuerier`, `KeysetSampler`, `RowCounter`, `RowCountEstimator`), so a large binary-`.db` table splits into N keyset/range chunks copied concurrently into the PG/MySQL target via the existing orchestrator (`internal/engines/sqlite/row_reader_batch.go` + `row_reader_range.go`). Single integer PK → MIN/MAX/divide; non-integer single / composite PK → `ROW_NUMBER()` keyset split-by-row-count. Exactly-once is collation-correct by construction (the Bug-74 class): row-value bounds (`(pk)>(?) AND (pk)<=(?)`, SQLite 3.15+) pushed into SQL, and WHERE / ORDER BY / sampler all reference the TABLE-QUALIFIED real PK columns so they share each column's intrinsic collation (BINARY / NOCASE / declared) with no injected `COLLATE` — pinned over a NOCASE TEXT PK, a BLOB PK, and a composite PK (unit exactly-once partition test + cross-engine chunked migration into PG). Each per-chunk reader opens its own read-only connection with a `busy_timeout` (concurrent-reader safety). The `.sql`-dump path STAYS single-reader (a dump materializes a temp DB the per-chunk readers would each re-materialize; `EstimateRowCount` returns 0 to route it single-reader); the `d1` query-API reader (already keyset-paginates) is untouched. A temporal (DATE/DATETIME/TIME) or decimal PK is EXCLUDED from the cursor path (chunk AND per-batch resume) — SQLite has no native temporal/decimal storage, so the decoded `time.Time`/decimal-string can't re-bind as the `>` cursor against the raw INTEGER/REAL/TEXT storage (silent truncation/dup); the reader vetoes it via a new optional `ir.BatchedReadDisqualifier` and falls back to whole-table single-reader (value-fidelity-review fix, pinned per encoding incl. the catastrophic unix-epoch INTEGER-storage case).

**Native D1 query-API reader — SHIPPED (ADR-0132).** A second source engine `d1` (registered alongside `sqlite`, same package, reusing `resolveColumnType` + the ADR-0129 date/bool policy + the shared `decodeCell` storage-class fidelity) reads a LIVE D1 over its HTTP query API and is the LOSSLESS D1 import.

**Schema-feature carry — SHIPPED (ADR-0133).** Both source readers (`sqlite` file/`.sql`, `d1` query-API) now CARRY generated columns, CHECK constraints, and partial/expression indexes into the IR's existing fields (`Column.GeneratedExpr`/`GeneratedStored`/`GeneratedExprDialect`, `Table.CheckConstraints`, `Index.Predicate`, `IndexColumn.Expression`), where previously they were silently omitted (generated columns landed as plain columns; CHECKs and partial/expression indexes were dropped). Generated columns come from `PRAGMA table_xinfo`'s `hidden` flag (2 VIRTUAL / 3 STORED) with the `AS (…)` body parsed from the `CREATE TABLE` SQL; CHECKs (table- and column-level, named/anonymous) and the partial-index `WHERE`/expression-index bodies are parsed by a shared SQLite-aware tokenizer (`internal/engines/sqlite/sql_features.go`) that skips strings/quoted-idents/comments so a keyword only matches standalone. Bodies are carried VERBATIM tagged dialect `"sqlite"`; the PG/MySQL writer dialect-guard (ADR-0133 §2) emits any non-{self,one-known-other} dialect verbatim, so a non-portable SQLite construct (`strftime`, …) is REJECTED LOUDLY at target DDL time rather than silently mistranslated, and a per-table/index WARN names every carried body. `SupportsCheckConstraint`/`SupportsGeneratedColumns` now declared true.

**SQLite→canonical (PG/MySQL) expression TRANSLATOR — SHIPPED (2026-07-03, ADR-0133 follow-up).** The verbatim tail is now *translated* rather than passed-through-and-warned. A shared `internal/translate.SQLiteExprToPG`/`SQLiteExprToMySQL` parses a SQLite expression body (its own minimal tokenizer — duplicated, not imported, to keep `internal/translate` free of an engine-package dependency) into a small AST over SQLite precedence and re-emits a value-fidelity-reviewed PROVABLY-portable subset fully parenthesised. **Allowlist:** column/literal refs; `+ - *`, all comparisons, `AND/OR/NOT`, `IS [NOT] NULL`; `||` concat (PG `||`, MySQL `CONCAT`); `/` on PG only (integer division matches SQLite; MySQL `/` is always decimal); abs/coalesce/ifnull→coalesce/nullif/length(PG LENGTH, MySQL CHAR_LENGTH)/1-arg trim·ltrim·rtrim; substr·substring with a LITERAL start ≥ 1 (negative counts from the end in SQLite); min·max→LEAST·GREATEST on MySQL only (LEAST/GREATEST propagate NULL like SQLite; PG's skip NULLs); cast AS text|real on both and cast AS numeric on PG only; CURRENT_TIMESTAMP·DATE·TIME. **Excluded** (each a proven silent-divergence a per-representative test would have passed): `%` on both (integer-coercion), upper/lower (ASCII vs Unicode fold), round (half-away vs half-even), cast AS integer (truncate vs round) / cast AS blob (byte semantics), plus strftime/julianday/unixepoch/date·time·datetime-with-args, glob/typeof/hex/…, the double-quoted misfeature, unknown functions → ok=false. **Non-portable policy is context-specific (F6):** a generated column and a CHECK are DATA-load-bearing, so a body with no provably-portable translation is REFUSED LOUDLY at the emit path (`refuseNonPortableSQLiteExpr{PG,MySQL}`, table/column-named) — NOT emitted verbatim, because a construct like `%` or MySQL `/` is syntactically valid on the target and would be SILENTLY accepted with divergent semantics (verbatim only loud-fails for non-portable *functions*). A non-portable partial/expression INDEX body is WARN-skipped (an index is a performance object). Wired into `translateGeneratedExpr`/`translateCheckExpr`/`translateIndexPredicate`/`translateIndexExpr` + `refuseUntranslatedCheckExpr*` + `emitColumnDef` in both engine `ddl_emit.go`/`schema_writer_check.go`; **src==dst value-ground-truthed** on real PG + MySQL (each kept construct's target-recomputed STORED gencol equals SQLite's computed value — incl. PG negative integer division, MySQL min/max NULL-propagation, multibyte length; every excluded construct aborts the migrate loudly on both the gencol and CHECK path). **Still DEFERRED:** `strftime`/epoch format-string + epoch-base translation (a wrong format silently corrupts a STORED gencol — out of scope) and a per-column encoding map. The empirical probe (2026-06-27) found BOTH default D1 paths round integers > 2^53 — `wrangler d1 export` rounds server-side (undetectable, before sluice runs) AND the default bare-JSON query API serialises through a double — so the only exact path is the query API reading each value as `typeof(c)` + `CASE typeof(c) WHEN 'blob' THEN hex(c) ELSE CAST(c AS TEXT) END`: integers come back as exact decimal text → exact `int64` (`9007199254740993` and max int64 round-trip exactly), `typeof` distinguishes INTEGER/REAL (default JSON collapses `1.0`→`1`), BLOBs decode from hex. Transport is plain `net/http` (no SDK); a non-2xx / `success:false` / `errors[]` is a loud error. DSN `d1://<account_id>/<database_id>` or `d1://<database_id>` (account from `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID`); token ENV-ONLY (`CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`), missing token/account/db refused loudly at open. Keyset pagination by PK (rowid fallback; `LIMIT/OFFSET` for a no-orderable-key table), table-qualified so the keyset orders the typed column not the CAST-text alias, bound sent as a string param so a > 2^53 bound isn't itself rounded. Migrate SOURCE only (`Capabilities.CDC = CDCNone`; write/CDC/snapshot Open* → wrapped not-implemented). Pinned by httptest unit tests: the big-int-exact headline, the typeof × shape decode matrix, date/bool over the text, schema from canned PRAGMA JSON, two-page keyset stitching, transport/DSN/secrets refusals. The export path stays the simple default for non-big-int / offline D1; `--source-driver d1` is the lossless choice for D1 with large integers. A live-D1 validation runs separately.


**Shipped (prototype).** `internal/engines/sqlite` — a read-only migrate source registered `sqlite`, pure-Go `modernc.org/sqlite` (no CGO), implementing `SchemaReader` + `RowReader`; the write/CDC/snapshot Open* return a wrapped `ErrNotImplemented`. Schema from `sqlite_master` + `PRAGMA table_info`/`foreign_key_list`/`index_list`/`index_info` → tables, columns, primary keys (INTEGER-PK rowid alias flagged auto-increment), foreign keys (implicit parent-PK references resolved), and plain-column secondary/unique indexes. Affinity → IR mapping (INTEGER→Integer, TEXT→Text, BLOB→Blob, REAL→Float, NUMERIC→Decimal-unconstrained); per-row storage-class fidelity enforced in the row reader — a value whose stored class can't be faithfully held in the column's resolved IR type is REFUSED LOUDLY (error names table/column/rowid/storage class), never coerced. DSN accepts a bare path, `file:` URI, or `sqlite://` URL, opened read-only via `_pragma=query_only(1)`. Pinned by a full affinity × storage-class decode matrix (pure + over a temp `.db`) and the cross-engine round-trip integration test proving SQLite→Postgres AND SQLite→MySQL (row counts + ordered value compare + type landing + FK). Wired into the CLI (`--source-driver sqlite`). **Declared date/bool policy — SHIPPED (ADR-0129).** A column DECLARED date/time/bool now resolves to the right IR type instead of NUMERIC→Decimal: case-insensitive substring precedence DATETIME/TIMESTAMP→`ir.Timestamp`, else DATE→`ir.Date`, else TIME→`ir.Time`, BOOL/BOOLEAN→`ir.Boolean` (an INTEGER 0/1 column is NOT guessed). The value encoding is an EXPLICIT operator choice — `--sqlite-date-encoding` (global) / `sqlite_date_encoding` DSN param (per-source): `iso` (default, ISO-8601 TEXT) / `unixepoch` / `unixmillis` (INTEGER/REAL) / `julian` (REAL/INTEGER) — refusing loudly on a storage-class mismatch (never a silently-wrong date), with `--type-override <col>=text` as the raw-carry escape hatch. modernc auto-converts TEXT in DATE/DATETIME/TIMESTAMP columns to `time.Time`; a `coalesce(col,col)` SELECT wart clears the decltype so sluice's own decode is authoritative. Pinned by the full {Date,Timestamp,Time}×{iso,unixepoch,unixmillis,julian}×{TEXT,INTEGER,REAL,BLOB,NULL} decode matrix + the boolean matrix + a real-driver julian/REAL ground truth + the cross-engine round-trip (iso + unixepoch into BOTH PG and MySQL). **Deferred (NOT yet built):** trigger-based CDC Phase 3 (the `sqlite-trigger` Phase 1 source AND the `d1-trigger` Phase 2 D1-over-HTTP source SHIPPED — see the SHIPPED notes above; Phase 3 = schema-change forwarding / capture-payload trimming / replica-aware poll; change-log retention Phase A `sluice trigger prune` IS now shipped — see the retention SHIPPED note above) and a per-column date-encoding map (the global flag + `--type-override` cover the common + outlier cases). (Within-table chunking for the binary `.db` path IS now shipped — see the SHIPPED note above; the `.sql`-dump path stays single-reader by design. CHECK constraints, generated columns, and partial/expression indexes ARE now read and carried — see the ADR-0133 SHIPPED note above.) **Validated end-to-end against REAL Cloudflare D1 (2026-06-26, shipped v0.99.141):** create→seed(DATE/DATETIME/BOOLEAN ISO + 0/1 + NULL + FK)→`wrangler d1 export --remote`→materialize via a one-line modernc `db.Exec(dump)`→migrate into PG16 + MySQL8, all PASS (DATE→date, DATETIME→timestamp, BOOLEAN→boolean/tinyint(1), exact rows, NULLs preserved, exactly-once). Real-D1 dump facts: a single `PRAGMA defer_foreign_keys=TRUE;` (loads fine), NO `_cf_KV` (current `d1 export` omits it), no BEGIN/COMMIT, no AUTOINCREMENT.

**Two ergonomic follow-ups the real-D1 run surfaced — both SHIPPED (ADR-0130):** (a) ✅ **direct `.sql`-dump ingest** — `migrate --source-driver sqlite --source dump.sql` now sniffs the SQLite magic header and, for a `.sql` TEXT dump, materializes it in-process into a temp SQLite DB via modernc (one multi-statement `Exec`, with a statement-split fallback; temp DB owned by the reader and removed on `Close`; malformed dump fails loudly naming the dump, no temp leak), so the D1 path is ONE command with no `sqlite3` CLI / Go shim; (b) ✅ **auto-skip `_cf_*` internal tables** — the schema reader's table list now excludes Cloudflare D1's `_cf_*` tables (escaped LIKE so a user table merely containing "cf" is never silently dropped) alongside `sqlite_*`, so no `--exclude-table _cf_KV` is needed. Pinned by unit tests (magic-sniff routing, `_cf_KV` skip, temp-lifecycle exists-while-open/gone-after-Close, malformed-dump loud-failure + no-leak, the statement splitter) + the cross-engine `.sql`-dump round-trip integration test into BOTH PG and MySQL (exact rows, `_cf_KV` does not land). The native D1 HTTP-API reader (the heavier, lossless-for-big-ints option) shipped later under ADR-0132 — see the SHIPPED note at the top of this item.

**Original design notes (below) retained for the deferred follow-ups.**

**Why.** A recurring ask is "import my SQLite / Cloudflare D1 database into Postgres or MySQL." `planetscale/cli` PR #1278 does this as an offline one-shot import from a **D1 SQLite export file** (not the live D1 API) into **PlanetScale Postgres only**, **no continuous sync**, by **wrapping pgloader** + a command suite. sluice's IR-first engine-registry architecture is built for this: a new source engine reuses the entire `Migrator` pipeline (parallel cold-copy, keyset chunker, type translation to **both** PG and MySQL, deferred index/constraint creation, `--dry-run`, `verify`, `diagnose`, loud-failure value discipline). `Capabilities.CDC = CDCNone` is a first-class migrate-only shape, and the code already anticipates SQLite (`capabilities.go`: `CDCTriggers // (e.g. SQLite future)`). It is among the cleanest possible engine adds — read-only, file-based, no replication, no roles — and gives a broader, dependency-free story than the PG-only pgloader wrapper.

**What.** A new `internal/engines/sqlite` source engine (registered `sqlite`), migrate-only: `SchemaReader` + `RowReader` (+ the chunker's row-count/range-bounds helpers) over the **pure-Go `modernc.org/sqlite` driver** (NO CGO — matches sluice's `CGO_ENABLED=0` posture; `mattn/go-sqlite3` is rejected for reintroducing CGO). Schema from `sqlite_master` + `PRAGMA table_info/foreign_key_list/index_list`. **Cloudflare D1 = consume a `wrangler d1 export` SQLite/SQL dump** (zero D1-specific code; it's just "a SQLite file"); a native D1 HTTP-API reader is a deferred later flavor. No new commands — reuse `sluice migrate` (+ `--dry-run`/`verify`/`diagnose`, which cover PR #1278's lint/verify/status equivalents); no pgloader dependency. See ADR-0128 for the full design.

**Gotchas.** The load-bearing part is **SQLite's dynamic typing**: a column's declared *affinity* (TEXT/NUMERIC/INTEGER/REAL/BLOB) is independent of each *row's* actual storage class, so a per-row storage-class mismatch (TEXT in an INTEGER column; a non-ISO string where the schema implies a date) must be **refused loudly, never silently coerced** (value-fidelity tenet, Bug-74 corollary — pin the class: each affinity × each actual storage class incl. NULL/mismatch × each target {PG, MySQL}, faithful-or-loud). SQLite has no native DATE/TIME/BOOL storage (dates are TEXT/INT/REAL by convention, bools are 0/1) — date/bool interpretation is an explicit *policy* (heuristic + override), not a silent guess. Needs a `value-fidelity-reviewer` pass before landing. Continuous SQLite→X sync (trigger-based CDC, the anticipated `CDCTriggers`) is a separate, larger, demand-gated follow-up — out of scope.

---

### 50. Carry user-defined triggers + event triggers across migrate / backup-restore / sync (operator-flagged 2026-06-30) — *RESEARCH / DESIGN-GATED; not started; needs further info before implementing; the Postgres→Postgres class is the prime motivator*

**Why.** sluice does NOT carry user objects that the IR doesn't model, and **triggers are one such gap** (confirmed by code: `internal/ir` has no `ir.Trigger` type / no `Table.Triggers` field — the only "Trigger" there is the `CDCTriggers` *strategy* enum; the native Postgres `SchemaReader` reads tables/columns/indexes/constraints/views but never `pg_trigger` / `pg_event_trigger`). So today, **regular table triggers AND `CREATE EVENT TRIGGER` objects are silently absent on the target** for every path: `migrate` (rebuilds schema from the IR), `backup`→`restore` (the logical backup stores the IR schema + rows, not a `pg_dump`), and `sync` CDC (PG logical replication doesn't stream DDL, and the ADR-0091 schema-forward classifier only forwards ADD/DROP/ALTER COLUMN + CREATE/DROP INDEX + CHECK — a `CREATE TRIGGER`/`EVENT TRIGGER` falls outside it and is not forwarded). For a **Postgres→Postgres** migration of a schema that leans on triggers (audit/`updated_at` stampers, denormalization keepers, or **event-trigger guards against accidental `DROP`/`TRUNCATE`**), the operator currently has to recreate every trigger out-of-band after the move — easy to forget, and a guard whose whole job is safety is exactly the thing you don't want silently missing. Worth carrying (at least for same-engine PG→PG), ideally with the IR-mediated discipline the rest of the schema uses.

**What (sketch — DESIGN-GATED, gather info first).** Add a trigger concept to the IR and wire PG read + emit: a `ir.Trigger` (table-scoped: name, timing/events, `FOR EACH ROW|STATEMENT`, `WHEN`, the called function, the verbatim body/definition) on `Table`, plus a schema-level / cluster-level `ir.EventTrigger` (name, event `ddl_command_start|end|sql_drop|table_rewrite`, filter tags, function). PG reader populates from `pg_trigger`/`pg_proc` (+ the trigger function source) and `pg_event_trigger`; PG writer emits `CREATE FUNCTION … RETURNS trigger` + `CREATE TRIGGER` / `CREATE EVENT TRIGGER` in the constraint/post-data phase. Start **Postgres→Postgres (same-engine) only**, where the trigger + its PL/pgSQL function body carry verbatim with no translation. Likely default **off / opt-in** initially (a forwarded/migrated trigger changes target write behavior — e.g. an audit trigger firing during a subsequent load), and surfaced loudly in the plan + `diagnose`.
