**Gotchas / open questions (the "further info needed" part).** (1) **Trigger FUNCTIONS are arbitrary PL/pgSQL** — carrying them verbatim is fine same-engine, but cross-engine (PG↔MySQL) is a translation problem far beyond sluice's expression translator; **scope to same-engine first**, and explicitly *refuse loudly* cross-engine rather than half-emit. (2) **Event triggers are CLUSTER-level, not schema objects** — they live outside the per-database/per-schema model sluice migrates, raise ownership/superuser-privilege questions on the target, and a `DROP`/`TRUNCATE`-guard event trigger could *block sluice's own target operations* (e.g. `--reset-target-data` DROPs, or a TRUNCATE in a reconcile path) — so emitting them needs an ordering/bypass story. (3) **Apply-time interaction:** sluice's CDC apply already *bypasses* target user-trigger enforcement during replay (Bug 164, `session_replication_role`) to avoid double-effects — so a carried trigger must NOT fire for sluice-applied changes; reconcile the "carry the object" goal with the "don't let it fire during our apply" reality. (4) **Dependency ordering:** a trigger depends on its function (+ possibly types/tables); emit in the right phase (after tables/data, with functions before triggers). (5) **Decide per-path scope:** migrate + backup/restore (static, lower-risk — carry as schema) vs sync (forward a mid-stream `CREATE TRIGGER` — interacts with ADR-0091 and is the riskier, demand-gated leg). (6) Needs a `value-fidelity`/`code-reviewer` pass and an ADR before implementing; this entry is the placeholder to collect the use cases + the same-engine-first design. Distinct from sluice's OWN capture triggers (`postgres-trigger`/`sqlite-trigger` CDC engines) — those are unrelated machinery.

### 51. Same-engine restore-parity oracle: diff sluice's PG→PG output against `pg_dump`/`pg_restore` (operator-flagged 2026-07-03) — *CORE SHIPPED v0.99.175 (`d24412fd`): `internal/pipeline/backup/dumpparity.go` comparator + allowlist, `TestMigrate_DumpParity_PGKitchenSink` Docker harness wired into the `pipeline-migrate` CI shard (`^TestMigrate_`), vacuous-pass floor guard; drove the standalone-sequence (`09e65f0a`) + UNIQUE-as-constraint (`58528d1b`) TRIAGE fixes. Phase 2 SHIPPED (`ea8c8cec`): `TestMigrate_DumpParity_MySQLKitchenSink` + `dumpparity_mysql.go` (MySQL-dialect parser decomposing mysqldump's inlined CREATE TABLE into per-element identity-keyed statements, `/*!80016*/` CHECK-guard unwrap, vacuous-pass floor), reusing the engine-neutral diff/allowlist core verbatim — in the `pipeline-migrate` CI shard. **Item 51 COMPLETE.** The MySQL oracle surfaced 2 cosmetic over-specification classes (redundant `CHARACTER SET/COLLATE` on default-equal columns + `USING BTREE` on indexes — stored schema identical, normalized fidelity-preservingly; a future cosmetic-emit-cleanup candidate, not a bug).*

**Why.** The Bug-74 lesson, generalized: hand-picked pins cannot enumerate the schema-feature surface, but `pg_dump` can — it is the reference implementation of "everything a PG schema can contain." Migrating the same source through sluice and through `pg_dump | pg_restore`, then diffing the two targets' catalogs, converts every unknown-unknown fidelity gap into a mechanical, reviewable list: each divergence is either a documented degradation (allowlisted, with a doc/ADR citation) or a latent bug — there is no third category. This is the single highest-leverage guard against the pre-promotion fear (a first user hitting an "obvious" gap we could have found ourselves), and it doubles as the evidence engine for extension-support prioritization: instead of guessing which extensions to add next (btree_gin/btree_gist, ltree, unaccent, …), the oracle run over real schemas (item 52) shows which features real sources actually contain. The `docs/cookbook/` pg_dump-comparison page already argues the concept; this item builds the harness.

**What.** An integration-tagged harness in `internal/pipeline` (`TestMigrate_DumpParity_*` names so it lands in the existing `pipeline-migrate` shard with no new CI axis): boot a source PG container seeded with a kitchen-sink schema; run sluice `migrate` PG→PG into target A; run `pg_dump | pg_restore` (executed *inside* the source container via docker exec, so the client version always matches the server) into target B on the same instance; `pg_dump --schema-only` both targets, split into statements, normalize whitespace, key by object identity, and diff the two statement sets. Any diff not covered by an explicit allowlist entry fails the test; every allowlist entry must cite the doc/ADR that declares the degradation. Kitchen-sink seed v1: partitioned tables, enums, domains, generated columns, identity + sequences, EXCLUDE constraints, partial + expression indexes, FK actions, comments, non-default collations; optional extension legs per the ADR-0032 catalog (hstore/citext/pgvector/pg_trgm, PostGIS under the postgis tag). Phase 2 (separate chunk): the MySQL→MySQL flavor with `mysqldump` as the oracle, and running the oracle over the item-52 corpus schemas.

**Gotchas / open questions.** (1) Raw text-diff of `pg_dump` output is ordering-fragile — compare statement *sets* keyed by object identity (kind + schema-qualified name), never line-diff the dumps. (2) A vacuous-pass guard is mandatory (the same lesson as `check-shard-coverage.sh`): if the normalizer/parser yields fewer objects than the seed declares, fail loudly — an empty diff because the comparator ate everything must not read as parity. (3) Item 50 (user triggers) will show up as a diff on day one — that is the harness *working*; allowlist it with a pointer to item 50 rather than weakening the comparator. (4) `pg_restore` needs `-Fc` (custom format) or use plain `psql` restore of a text dump — pick one and pin it; text + `psql -v ON_ERROR_STOP=1` is simpler and version-stable. (5) Sequence *values* (`setval`) differ legitimately when sluice copies data and pg_dump does schema-only legs — compare schema-only on both sides and cover row parity with the existing `verify` machinery instead. (6) Keep the allowlist in a reviewable data file next to the test, not inline table-driven cases, so "what do we knowingly not carry?" stays a one-file answer — that file is also the honest input to the docs' limitations section.

### 52. Real-schema corpus harness: migrate popular OSS app schemas on a schedule (operator-flagged 2026-07-03) — *HARNESS SHIPPED-IN-SUBSTANCE + IN CI: `migrate_realworld_corpus_integration_test.go` (13 corpora — GitLab/WordPress/Joomla/MediaWiki/Chinook/Employees/Vitess) + `..._congruence_integration_test.go` (matched-pair oracle) + vendored real dumps under `testdata/real-world-corpus/`, run in the `^TestMigrate_` shard. FINISHING TOUCHES SHIPPED: (1) scheduled weekly `extended-suites.yml` `corpus` leg (fetch-on-demand dumps + `-run '^TestMigrate_Corpus_'`; also compiles in the per-PR pipeline-migrate shard but SKIPs there since the dumps are gitignored); (2) sample-row `verify` legs (`TestMigrate_Corpus_SampleVerify_Chinook_{MySQLToMySQL,PGToPG}` — real same-engine migrate of a small deterministic seed + count-depth + sample-depth verify, vacuous-pass guarded on SampleSize); (3) the item-51 restore-parity oracle over the corpus (`TestMigrate_Corpus_DumpParity_Chinook_{PGToPG,MySQLToMySQL}` + `backup.DumpParityCorpusAllowlist{PG,MySQL}` class-keyed globs — Chinook is FULL PARITY except sluice's own state tables). REMAINING (deferred, reported): broadening the dump-parity oracle to MediaWiki/Joomla/WordPress needs a body-equivalence pairing pass in the identity-keyed comparator — sluice's deliberate `pgIndexName` qualification (GitHub #26) diverges every short-named index's IDENTITY, which the glob-key allowlist can't safely express (a blanket `CREATE INDEX *` would mask a genuinely dropped index). FLAGGED FINDING from the MediaWiki MySQL→MySQL leg (surfaced, then descoped): sluice's re-emit of `logging.log_timestamp BINARY(14) DEFAULT '19700101000000' NOT NULL` fails on the MySQL target with Error 1067 "Invalid default value" though the identical source DDL loads clean — a candidate same-engine BINARY-column-default fidelity bug to triage.*

**Why.** Real applications concentrate exactly the weird-but-common DDL a first user brings — fulltext indexes, enum defaults, partial indexes, odd collations, gencol idioms — and no generative fuzzer or hand-built kitchen-sink reproduces their distribution. Every corpus failure is, by construction, something a real user would have hit; that makes the corpus the most honest pre-promotion gate the project can buy. Complements item 51 (which enumerates *feature* fidelity) with ecological validity, and its schemas become item 51's oracle inputs.

**What.** A `testdata`-style corpus directory of schema-only dumps with provenance notes (upstream project, version, how regenerated), seeded with 3–4: WordPress/WooCommerce (MySQL), GitLab (PG — the case-study doc already exists), Keycloak (PG), and a Django or Rails skeleton app. Harness migrates each across a starter direction set (PG→PG, MySQL→MySQL, MySQL→PG) with a small seeded sample of rows, runs `verify`, and — once item 51 lands — runs the restore-parity oracle on the same-engine legs. Cadence: a weekly `extended-suites.yml` leg plus the pre-release regression cycle. Failures get filed with the schema name as the reproducer.

**Gotchas / open questions.** (1) Provenance/licensing: prefer *regenerating* schemas from upstream installers inside containers (documented recipe per schema) over vendoring dumps whose redistribution status is murky; the corpus dir stores what we ran and how to rebuild it. (2) Corpus rot: pin upstream versions and refresh deliberately (a corpus that silently tracks upstream HEAD makes failures ambiguous — upstream change vs sluice regression). (3) Keep runtime bounded: schema + small sample rows, never full datasets; the corpus tests fidelity, not throughput. (4) Direction-matrix explosion is real — start with the three directions above and grow on demand. (5) Some schemas need engine features sluice deliberately refuses (e.g. triggers, item 50) — those refusals must be *named* in the harness output as expected, same allowlist discipline as item 51.

### 53. Cookbook-as-executable-tests: every documented recipe runs against the released binary (operator-flagged 2026-07-03) — *FIRST CUT SHIPPED (`27302400`): assertion-bearing sidecar `.sh` for the 3 highest-traffic recipes (`docs/cookbook/{quickstart,recipe-migrate-once,recipe-backup-encrypted}.sh` + `_cookbook-lib.sh`) + a sluice-testing runner (`workspace/cookbook/run-cookbook.sh`, all 3 GREEN vs the v0.99.185 binary + local rig). Immediately caught real drift: `docs/examples/quickstart.md` §4b's sample DRY-RUN banner is stale vs the binary's structured slog (`msg="dry run: migration plan" tables=N` / `msg="dry run: table" name=…`) — behavior pinned, doc-sample refresh pending. Batch 2 (`b9578a3f`) added redaction-keyset + bidirectional-cutover + broker-replay (all GREEN; postgis/heroku SKIP-excluded — cloud/PostGIS deps), and the runner is wired into the regression cycle's "clean" gate (regression-cycle-runner step 5). Batch 2 caught **two more real doc bugs**: (1) `recipe-redaction-keyset.md`'s keyset YAML used a flat `keys:` map the binary rejects — FIXED to the nested `keyset: keys: - name/active/generations` shape; (2) `recipe-bidirectional-cutover.md` documents `sync start --resume` (no such flag, exit 80) and a migrate→sync gapless handoff that actually cold-start-refuses on the populated target — the real gapless path is `sync start`'s own integrated cold-start (`docs/snapshot-cdc-handoff.md`). **BOTH doc rewrites now DONE:** quickstart §4b → real slog sample (`84c8e708`); cutover recipe → rewritten to the correct self-contained gapless `sync start` model (no separate `migrate`, no nonexistent `--resume`), fixing 3 further stale flags in-pass (`sync health --max-stale-seconds`, `cutover --sequence-margin`, required `--target-driver`), sidecar re-validated green (`90dad1b7`). **Item 53 doc-drift loop CLOSED — all 4 recipe bugs the tests caught are fixed.** REMAINING = covering more recipes as demand warrants.*

**Why.** The specific nightmare is "the thing the docs told the user to do fails." Recipes rot silently today: flags get renamed, defaults change, and only a human re-walking the page notices. The post-release regression cycle (sluice-testing) exercises focus areas but not the documented recipes *verbatim* — so the surface users actually start from is the least-tested surface in the project.

**What.** Each `docs/cookbook/` recipe gains a runnable sidecar script (explicit `.sh` next to the page — not markdown-fence extraction, which is fragile) that executes the recipe's commands against the *released binary* and asserts the documented outcome. The post-release regression cycle runs the full set; any failure blocks the "cycle clean" verdict. Start with the three highest-traffic pages: the quickstart, one-shot migrate, and the encrypted backup chain. The runner lives in the sluice-testing cycle (which already stages the release binary); the scripts live in this repo next to the docs they pin, so a docs PR that changes a recipe must update its script in the same diff.

**Gotchas / open questions.** (1) Recipes with cloud dependencies (KMS, PlanetScale, D1) need local substitutions (localstack leg, or marked operator-only and excluded from the automated set — but then say so in the page header). (2) Keep scripts assertion-bearing (exit codes + a named expected artifact/output), not just "commands ran" — a recipe test that only checks exit 0 is the no-error-assertion anti-pattern. (3) Drift direction matters: the script pins the *docs*, CI pins the *code* — when they disagree the fix may be either; the failure message should say "recipe page X step N" so triage starts at the right file.

### 54. Large-dataset performance program: pgcopydb-gap items + cross-mode parity backlog (operator-flagged 2026-07-04) — *RESEARCH COMPLETE; matrix + checker agent SHIPPED; implementation backlog open*

**Why.** Two operator asks converge here: close the remaining PG→PG gap with pgcopydb for very large imports, and structurally prevent the "optimized in migrate but not sync/backup" class. The research (`docs/research/perf-gap-analysis-2026-07.md`) found the pgcopydb software gap is small (last measured 1.33–1.42× pre-buffered-pipe-fix; the 2 TB/hr headline is Metal infrastructure) with one big structural remainder (inline-PK maintenance vs pgcopydb's post-load parallel PK sort), confirmed PlanetScale-MySQL write levers are structurally exhausted except round-trip amortization, and inventoried 11 accidental cross-mode asymmetries (`docs/dev/perf-parity-matrix.md` — the living matrix; `perf-parity-checker` agent + CLAUDE.md working agreement enforce it going forward).

**What (the ranked backlog — each item lands with its matrix-row update per the working agreement).** Quick wins (S) — **ALL DONE**: ~~buffer the restore/chain-replay/broker channels (matrix gap 2) + redact/shard tees (gap 6)~~ — **DONE (2026-07)**: all three replay hops + both tees carry the shared `rowChanBuffer` (64) — matrix gaps 2 and 6 closed; ~~chain-replay one-chunk prefetch (gap 4)~~ — **DONE (2026-07, replay-path hardening chunk)**: `streamIncrementalChanges` read-ahead fetcher (fetch+SHA-verify N+1 while N applies), gap 4 closed; ~~`--analyze-after` post-load target ANALYZE~~ — **DONE (`c98f9dec`)**: opt-in `--analyze-after` via `ir.TableAnalyzer` on all 3 target engines, advisory per-table WARN (`pipeline/analyze_after.go`, matrix row 16); ~~shared exported snapshot for migrate's parallel PG readers (consistency win + CTID prerequisite; release at copy-phase end)~~ — **DONE (`31d2afd0`)**: PG-source `SnapshotExporter` + importer-pinned pool/chunk readers, released at copy-phase end, WARN-fallback to per-conn views (`pipeline/migrate_snapshot.go`, `postgres/snapshot_exporter.go`, matrix row 15). Medium: ~~sync cold-start parallelism defaults for MySQL-binlog/VStream sources (gap 3)~~ — **DONE (survey-first defaults chunk, 2026-07-04)**: MySQL-binlog default flipped to auto min(4, tables) (`defaultNativeCopyTableParallelism`, ADR-0101 impl note — consistency-identical FTWRL cut, loud serial fallback on no-RELOAD sources, `=1` opt-out); VStream surveyed and DELIBERATELY kept 1 (un-persisted K would silently re-partition a durable-watermark resume across an upgrade — ADR-0099 impl note; the sequential path now INFO-names the knob); trigger flavors got the serial INFO line (parallelizing them = separate L item); ~~backup within-table read chunking (gap 1 — the single-huge-table backup ceiling; needs per-table snapshot consistency)~~ — **DONE (ADR-0149, 2026-07-04)**: eligible tables split into PK ranges read off the same exported snapshot (`backup full --bulk-parallelism`, PG lazy-snapshot path; MySQL-eager/fallback/SQLite/VStream = cited deliberate absences; incl. the 59c55e27 estimator fix on the backup snapshot readers); ~~PS byte-targeted ~1 MB INSERT batching (the one real PS write lever; AIMD owns the ceiling, flush on the 20 s tx budget) + a tier-CPU-ceiling operator hint~~ — **DONE (ADR-0150, 2026-07-04)**: both batched-INSERT bulk conn loops (plain + idempotent + the ADR-0097/0102 fan-outs) flush on an estimated ~1 MiB statement byte target (the pscale-dumper size, = ADR-0139's coalescing constant) with the row cap raised to a 10k safety ceiling + a 60k placeholder bound; autocommit-per-statement keeps every tx far inside the 20 s killer (nothing groups statements per tx); AIMD/budgets untouched; hosted-PlanetScale targets get a once-per-writer tier-CPU-bound INFO (self-hosted vitess excluded). Large, ADR-first: opt-in `--deferred-pk` post-copy PK build (biggest 1 TB lever; conflicts with resume/CDC-handoff dup protection — gate to one-shot migrate); CTID-range chunking for PK-less tables (after the shared snapshot). Evidence-gated: PS Imports/VReplication head-to-head benchmark; scoped bulk-load GUC bundle (`synchronous_commit=off` copy-session-only — must be provably unable to leak into the CDC applier's F7 pin).

**Gotchas.** (1) The deferred-PK mode is the one item with real correctness interplay — own ADR, value-fidelity review, and the restore-parity oracle must stay green with it on. (2) Backup chunking must hold a per-table consistent view (exported snapshot / FTWRL surfaces exist from ADR-0084 gating). (3) Every S item here is behavior-neutral except throughput — pin with the existing benchmarks/ harnesses, record numbers in the CHANGELOG per house style. (4) Deliberate absences in the matrix (olap-off-chunked-reads Bug 132, MySQL coalescing-not-pipelining; the VStream unbuffered drain was retired from this list by the 2026-07-08 audit P′-1 fix — buffered 64 + batched pops) are cited — do not "fix" them without revisiting the rationale.

### 55. Flat-file sources: mydumper/pscale-dump dirs, CSV/TSV/NDJSON, Parquet (operator-flagged 2026-07-04) — *RESEARCH COMPLETE (`docs/research/flat-file-sources.md`); implementation not started*

**Why.** Provider-only-gives-dumps migrations (PlanetScale's own export IS mydumper format), air-gapped moves, and spreadsheet-to-database onboarding all start from a file, not a live DSN. The research found the answer is per-format: mydumper/`pscale database dump` dirs are regular enough for a native reader (per-table single-CREATE-TABLE schema files + INSERT-only data chunks); CSV/TSV/NDJSON fit the existing stage-into-SQLite + `--infer-types` machinery verbatim; Parquet carries its own typed schema; plain mysqldump/pg_dump `.sql` and `-Fc` are a full-dialect-grammar / private-format trap that gets loud refusal + a scratch-server recipe instead. Prior art validates the caution: pgloader deliberately parses no SQL dumps.

**What (phases, from the research doc).** P1 (M): `mydumper` source-only engine (d1 registry shape) — schema from per-table `*-schema.sql` (bounded MySQL CREATE TABLE parse; needs an ADR blessing the contained DDL-parse exception, ADR-0133 precedent), data streamed from INSERT-VALUES chunks + gz/zstd; silent-loss pin matrix = every value family × escape shape (no-hex-blob backslash binary, `0x…`, `SET NAMES`, NULL vs `'NULL'`) ground-truthed against a myloader-restored database. P2 (S/M): CSV/TSV/NDJSON via the ADR-0130 materialize path + auto-engaged `--infer-types`; explicit `--csv-null`/header/encoding flags — never sniffed (RFC 4180 has no NULL representation; the #1 silent-loss class); JSON numbers as raw text (the D1 int64>2^53 lesson). P3 (S): signature-detect plain `.sql`/`PGDMP` at open → loud refusal naming the scratch-server-replay recipe. P4 (M, demand-gated): Parquet reader off the vetted CGO-free parquet-go. Non-goals: parsing pg_dump DDL/-Fc, DuckDB dependency (CGO), subsuming the backup format.

**Gotchas.** (1) The P1 DDL parse is the tenet-sensitive piece — scope it to the single-CREATE-TABLE-per-file shape and refuse anything else loudly; the ADR must draw that line. (2) mydumper `metadata` carries binlog pos/GTID — a future dump→CDC handoff hook; record it, don't build it. (3) Verify semantics for file sources = re-scan (count depth cheap; sample depth needs the per-chunk addressing only chunked formats give). (4) Staging typed dumps through SQLite is forbidden (DECIMAL/uint64/temporal degradation — the research doc's option-b analysis); staging is for schema-less input only.

### 56. AI agent-skills pack: reusable operator playbooks over the AI-friendly surface (operator-flagged 2026-07-05) — *SHIPPED: 9 skills + `install.sh` (`skills/`), the CI doc-sync guard (`scripts/check-skills-flags.sh` in the Lint job), the AGENTS.md cross-link, and the sluicesync.com "Drive sluice from an AI agent" guide. The doc-sync guard covers both flags AND subcommands. Remaining = Tier-2 refinement / new skills on demand. Proposal: `docs/research/ai-skills-pack.md`*

**Why.** Prompted by [`planetscale/skills`](https://github.com/planetscale/skills) — open agent-skills (`SKILL.md`, the vendor-neutral convention Claude Code/Cursor load) whose spine is *read-only assessment → evidence-backed proposal → approval-gated execution*. That spine **is** sluice's identity (correctness/trust gate throughput; validate end-to-end; loud failure; contain-PG-complexity), and the substrate already shipped in v0.99.175 (`AGENTS.md`, `llms.txt`, JSON envelopes on migrate/sync/backup/restore, `SLUICE-E-*` codes + `docs/operator/error-codes.md`, the exit taxonomy). Skills are the next layer up: task-scoped playbooks that consume that structured surface with little-to-no new product code, and they differentiate — not "operate a database" but "**migrate/sync without silently corrupting data**," a pre-flight → execute → verify loop with loud-failure recovery baked in.

**What (from the research doc).** A top-level `skills/` dir (open convention, plain `SKILL.md` + sibling-relative refs, cross-linked from `AGENTS.md`/site nav). Catalog, ranked by fit: **Tier 1** — `migrate-preflight` (drive `migrate --dry-run` JSON + type-mapping/capability/RLS/ownership/keyless preflights → go/no-go with risks named), `fidelity-verify` (verify/reconcile + the `value-types.md` contract, Bug-74 pin-the-*family* discipline as an operator check), `sluice-error-triage` (map `SLUICE-E-*` + exit code → root cause + recovery off the error-codes doc), `backup-chain-operator` (full→incr→compact→prune→restore-test, incl. the `--encrypt-mode` per-chunk/per-chain rules — the Bug 179 footgun; Class-style gate on the destructive legs). **Tier 2** — `cdc-sync-operator`, `planetscale-migration` (the `--source-driver planetscale`/VStream + reparent/ownership gotchas), `fleet-operator`. Borrow PlanetScale's read-back-to-verify success criteria, approval gates for destructive ops, evidence-backed report templates, and risk-acknowledged autonomous mode. **Sequencing:** ship `migrate-preflight` + `sluice-error-triage` first (cheapest, self-contained, no new product code), validate the format, then the rest of Tier 1, Tier 2 on demand.

**Gotchas / open questions.** (1) 1.0 scope — two-skill PoC to prove the format vs the full Tier-1 set (recommend PoC first). (2) Governance depth — full Class A–E vs a lighter "destructive vs read-only" two-tier gate matching sluice's existing loud-refusal boundary (lean two-tier). (3) **Drift coupling** — a skill naming flags/commands can rot; add a lightweight doc-sync guard (the `llms.txt`-from-NAV / error-codes bidirectional-test pattern) so a renamed flag fails a test, not a user's session. (4) In-repo `skills/` (versioned with the CLI it drives — recommended, enables the doc-sync coupling) vs a sibling `sluicesync/skills` repo (PlanetScale's choice).

---

### Deferred audit findings (2026-07-08 cross-check)

From `workspace/repo-audit-2026-07-08-fable-crosscheck.md` (§4, N-numbered; that file is gitignored scratch, so each entry below is self-contained). These were deliberately NOT fixed in the 2026-07-08 docs/CI-hygiene wave; each is a fix window awaiting scheduling.

- ~~**N-8 + N-9 — backup-encryption integrity hardening (MEDIUM security cluster; design once, FormatVersion bump).**~~ — **IMPLEMENTED (ADR-0152, 2026-07-08; pending review/release).** FormatVersion 5: GCM AAD binds every encrypted chunk to (manifest identity + path [+ list ordinal for change chunks — replay order is semantic]); chain-CEK wraps identity-bound via `crypto.BoundEnvelope` (AWS EncryptionContext / GCP AAD / passphrase GCM AAD; Azure deliberately not faked — no API parameter, documented); Azure key-version pinned + recorded in KEKRef and rebound on unwrap (N-9), lying comment fixed; restore validates chunk headers against the manifest schema (comment 3 made true); chain-restore verifies SchemaHash (comment 4 made true; fulls now record it; sequence-refresh re-stamps it; pre-v5-sequences WARN carve-out). Pre-v5 chains restore byte-identically (version-gated legacy path; pinned); pre-v5 encrypted RESUME inherits the unbound shape. Tamper matrix + per-family crypto/codec pins landed. Residual (documented, out of scope): the manifest is unsigned — whole-backup rollback / tail truncation need a signed-manifest design. N-9's real-AKV live pin remains open (unit-level fake reproduces the no-version-metadata semantics; validate against real AKV before relying on it in anger). *Original why:* the encrypted-backup path currently provides confidentiality only, while two in-code comments and SECURITY.md's shared-storage framing imply integrity that doesn't exist. Verified: `gcm.Seal(nonce, nonce, plaintext, nil)` / `gcm.Open(nil, nonce, ct, nil)` — nil AAD (`internal/crypto/envelope.go:294,320`); zero KMS `EncryptionContext` anywhere in `internal/crypto`; `ChunkReader.Header()` has no non-test callers despite `pipeline/blobcodec/backup_chunk.go:50-56` claiming a column-rename "surfaces as a header mismatch on restore"; `Manifest.SchemaHash` is computed+written at 3 sites and compared nowhere despite `ir/backup/manifest.go:454-459` claiming chain-restore uses it as a tamper sanity check. Per-chain mode shares one CEK, so any valid chunk decrypts wherever a rewritten manifest points — chunk splice/rollback/omission on shared storage. *What:* GCM AAD = BackupID + chunk index; KMS EncryptionContext on wrap/unwrap; actually validate the chunk header on restore; actually compare SchemaHash in chain-restore — as one FormatVersion-bumping design. **Fixing the two lying comments is part of this item** (at minimum, if the integrity work is re-deferred, correct the comments to say what the code does). Grouped in: **N-9** — Azure Key Vault unwrap targets the *latest* key version and discards the WrapKey response `KID` (`internal/crypto/azure_kms.go:263-285`; the in-code comment asserts Azure recovers the wrap-time version from blob metadata — that is AWS/GCP behavior, Azure KW ciphertext carries none), so enabling key auto-rotation (common policy) makes restores of older chains fail with a misleading "wrong key or tampered". Persist the WrapKey response KID as the unwrap target. *Gotchas:* existing chains must keep restoring (Bug 116's FormatVersion loud-refusal discipline); per-chunk vs per-chain CEK modes differ in splice exposure; N-9 is derived from Azure API semantics, not live-run — pin against real AKV (or a recorded fixture) before shipping.
- **N-5 ✅ RESOLVED — REFUTED live (2026-07-08); the "one-sided fix" is correct-by-construction, now pinned + documented.** The Phase-A ground truth (real MySQL 8.0.46 + 8.4.10, {default, NBE} read session × {default, NBE} creation session, per-cell `@@SESSION.sql_mode` asserted) showed ALL FOUR cells byte-identical: SHOW CREATE TABLE and information_schema COLUMN_TYPE always print literals with the fixed escape set `\0 \n \r \\` + doubled `''` (0x08/0x09/0x1A/`"`/0x7F raw) — NO_BACKSLASH_ESCAPES changes only the PARSE direction (why the emit side threads `backslashIsMySQLEscape`), never the PRINT direction. So the unconditional recovery decoders are correct in every reachable mode, and the audit's proposed fix (threading sqlMode into the decode) would itself have corrupted (`'C:\\temp'` read "raw" under NBE → two backslashes). Landed instead: the live family × mode pin `TestSchemaLiteralDecode_SQLModeMatrix_ByteExact` (mysql engine integration; binary defaults quoted+hex, ENUM+SET labels, table comment incl. NUL-recovery, column comment, VARCHAR default — each under {default, NBE} reader sessions via the real `WithSQLMode` plumbing, session mode asserted on the reader's own connection), plus the named invariant ("mode-independent print discipline") in `binary_default_recovery.go` / `types.go` / `connect.go` so nobody "completes" the one-sided fix later. The pin fails loudly if a future MySQL starts printing mode-dependently.
- **N-15 — MySQL perf-parity pair (cite the perf-parity-matrix working agreement; both land with matrix-row updates).** ~~(a) Production MySQL DSNs never set `interpolateParams` and there is no statement cache, so every parameterized Exec pays a hidden server-side PREPARE round-trip — 2 RTTs where 1 would do, up to ~2× CDC apply latency at PlanetScale RTTs (`mysql/connect.go`, `change_applier_multirow.go:411,434`). Fix shape: a per-conn prepared-statement cache keyed (table, shape, row-count) — NOT interpolation (the value-fidelity choice stands).~~ **(a) IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-08 (ADR-0153, unreleased) — as flavor-default INTERPOLATION, not the cache:** the audit's fidelity objection did not survive the 2026-07-08 real-PS bench (byte-exact on 9 families; −33% bulk copy, −26% CDC burst drain, p95 flush −105 ms ≈ exactly 1 RTT) + the Phase-1 Bug-74 matrix (every family × protocol × {bulk INSERT, CDC multirow} pinned byte-exact on real MySQL before the flip, catching + closing two real divergences: NaN/±Inf → SLUICE-E-VALUE-UNREPRESENTABLE pre-driver refusal; float64 −0.0 → `'-0'` string encoding against MySQL's `-0`-literal sign mangle). PlanetScale/Vitess flavors default `interpolateParams=true` at the `parseDSNForFlavor` choke point; vanilla stays binary (deliberate; DSN opt-in documented in throughput-tuning); explicit DSN wins (raw-DSN explicitness detection); NBE ground-truthed correct in-driver (pinned, no guard); unsafe-collation default steps aside with WARN; packet headroom pinned (driver ErrSkip → prepared fallback at the boundary). Perf-parity-matrix row 18 declares the cells. A vanilla-side stmt-cache remains available if evidence ever appears. Two INFO-grade residuals from the round-2 fidelity review, carried here so they don't vanish: (G4) ~~the VStream COPY/CDC path decodes FLOAT through its OWN gRPC field carrier — entirely outside the SQL read projection this chunk fixed — pre-existing and unaudited for the same float32-carrier precision class (informational; audit if a VStream FLOAT fidelity report ever surfaces)~~ **RESOLVED by vttestserver ground truth (2026-07-09, `TestVStream_FloatCarrierParity`): the CDC (binlog row-event) leg is float32-EXACT — vttablet re-encodes the binlog float32 bits as shortest-round-trip text (`'E', -1, 32`), so only the float64 carrier's low bits differ from the SQL reader's float64(float32(x)), observable solely by a double-width target — the informational, confirmed and pinned at the float32-exactness bar; the COPY leg, however, surfaced a REAL float32-level silent loss (mysqld display rounding), promoted to its own open-bugs entry (2026-07-09) below**; and the pgtrigger string-"NaN" bypass documented in ADR-0153 (loud, non-retriable, just less well-named). (b) The MySQL index-overlap path lacks the ADR-0114 reparent-transient retry the PG overlap has (`postgres/schema_writer_index_overlap.go:207,229` wraps builds; the MySQL overlap calls `buildTableIndexes` bare and the writer's own `IsTransientError` goes unused on the branch every production PlanetScale/Vitess target now takes since v0.99.199/200) — a storage-grow reparent mid-`ALTER` aborts the migrate (loud; `--resume` recovers) on precisely the platform where reparents happen. **(b) IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-08 (unreleased):** both MySQL overlap paths now wrap the per-table build in the ADR-0108-envelope reparent retry (`mysql/schema_writer_index_reparent_retry.go` — same classifier + wall-clock budget as the cold-copy flush retry; fresh-conn reacquire on the worker path, implicit pool reacquire on the serial VStream path; detect-then-skip makes the replay double-create-safe), with perf-parity-matrix row 17 declaring the coverage.
- ~~**N-16 — pgtrigger change-log index diet (source-write amplification on managed tiers).**~~ — **IMPLEMENTED (2026-07-09; pending review/release).** Query-inventory re-verified at fix time: nothing reads either index (poll/anchor/settle-clamp/prune/stats key on `id` + `txid` alone; the sqlite-trigger sibling never had them). Setup no longer creates them and emits idempotent `DROP INDEX IF EXISTS` for both names so any pre-existing install converges on the next setup run (no schema_version migration — pre-production simplification per operator). The capture trigger's per-fired-row PK catalog lookup is replaced by the ADR-0066 §3 TG_ARGV[0] JSON-array bake (composite PKs in conkey order); a stale bake after a post-setup PK ALTER refuses writes loudly via a projection guard (the event-trigger tier already refuses at the ALTER's op='X' row). ADR-0066 impl-notes carry the full posture; unit + integration pins incl. composite-PK end-to-end across all three payload modes and the pre-N-16 convergence re-run. *Original why:* `pgtrigger/setup.go` created `sluice_change_log_id_idx ON (id)` — an exact duplicate of the PK's implicit index — and `sluice_change_log_table_idx ON (schema_name, table_name, id)`, which no query used: two useless indexes maintained on every captured source DML, on tiers where the operator pays IOPS; plus the PK column list re-derived from catalogs per fired row.
- ~~**N-14 — `--rebuild-catalog` stamps `DefaultCodec` on rebuilt lineage regardless of actual chunk compression (wrong-heal on the DR path).**~~ — **IMPLEMENTED (2026-07-09; pending review/release).** The rebuilt record's codec is now SNIFFED from chunk magic bytes and VERIFIED across the chain (`blobcodec.SniffCodec` + `lineage.SniffChainCodec` — one probe per manifest; the sniff is deterministic because a chunk's codec input always begins with the header line's `{`, so zstd `28 B5 2F FD` / gzip `1F 8B` / none `{` are disjoint). Sniff-and-verify posture on the durable-record path (`RebuildLineageCatalogAt`): mixed probes, unknown magic, truncated/unreadable chunks all REFUSE loudly. Chunk-layout finding that shaped the encrypted leg: the codec sits INSIDE the encryption envelope (`ChunkWriter` compresses then encrypts on Close), so encrypted chunks carry no codec magic on disk — a keyless rebuild refuses (wraps `lineage.ErrCodecSniffEncrypted`, steering to `--encrypt`) and a keyed rebuild decrypts one chunk (same `UnwrapChainCEK`/AAD chokepoints as restore) and sniffs the plaintext; `backup verify --rebuild-catalog` builds the read envelope from the existing `EncryptionFlags`. `ResolveLineage`'s synthetic root gets the same sniff, best-effort (its result is in-memory, re-derived per call — on probe failure/encrypted-without-keys it WARNs naming the DefaultCodec assumption instead of hard-failing, so keyless flows like SHA-only verify keep working; a wrong assumption still fails loudly at first chunk decode). DefaultCodec survives only as the nothing-to-probe (chunk-less chain) fallback, WARN-named on both paths. Pinned: magic-table + every-codec-family real-writer bytes + encrypted-layout unit pins (blobcodec), rebuild/synthetic family pins + mixed-codec refusal + truncated refusal + encrypted keyless-refuse/keyed-sniff (lineage), and the DR scenario end-to-end per codec family incl. the encrypted leg (`TestBackupRebuildCatalog_*`, pipeline integration). *Original why:* `pipeline/lineage/chain_catalog.go` recorded `blobcodec.DefaultCodec` (zstd) never-sniffed on rebuild and on the synthetic root, and restore trusts the record — a gzip/none-era chain whose `lineage.json` was lost got a rebuilt catalog that lied, and restore failed with a bare zstd decode error whose remediation hint pointed back at the same rebuild tool.
- ✅ **FIXED (in review, 2026-07-09) — N-17 — testing-guard blind spots beyond the known manifest drift.** (a) `check-run-filter-coverage.sh` now auto-discovers the tag-axis set from `*_test.go` `//go:build` lines (vet-tags-style GOOS/GOARCH stripping) and fails on any tag with neither a MANIFEST axis nor a documented `EXEMPT_TAGS` entry (psverify/jsonbench/compressbench, each with a rationale in the header; a stale exemption also fails) — a future `integration && newtag` suite can no longer type-check, pass both coverage guards, and run in no workflow. Plus the hand-copied-mirror tripwire: every MANIFEST regex must appear verbatim (fixed-string grep) in the workflow file its leg label names, so a `-run` filter edited on one side fails the Lint job (documented limitation: a stale regex surviving in a YAML comment could mask drift; full YAML parsing wasn't worth it in a POSIX-sh guard). (b) `check-shard-coverage.sh`'s matching now mirrors ci.yml's actual package listing — bare entries (`internal/pipeline`, `internal/pipeline/backup`) are NON-recursive like the `./pkg/` go-test arguments; `/...` entries cover subtrees — pinned by an always-run `self_test` whose load-bearing case asserts `internal/pipeline` does NOT cover `internal/pipeline/migcore` (verified latent at fix time: no integration tests exist under any pipeline subpackage except the guarded set). Both (a) and (b) were also proven by staged fake-escapee negative runs. (c) The `kmsverify` scaffolding is wired for real: round-trip, chain extension (the Bug-43 salt hazard has no KMS analog — the same envelope extends the chain, no rebuild hook), and the wrong-key + missing-key loud refusals now run against a real localstack KMS container + real PG under `integration && kmsverify`, with a weekly + dispatch `kmsverify` leg in extended-suites.yml and a matching run-filter-guard MANIFEST axis; only the IAM access-denied case remains an honest skip (localstack community edition doesn't enforce IAM — that branch stays unit-pinned in `internal/crypto/aws_kms_test.go`).
- ~~**N-11 — fleet zero-coercion defeats the documented "0 disables" semantics (the zero-value-collapse class on the fleet layer).**~~ — **IMPLEMENTED (2026-07-09; pending review/release).** The full `firstNonZero*` audit of the fleet spec→Streamer mapping classified every coerced field: class (a) — 0 is documented-meaningful on the CLI (`--apply-exec-timeout` / `--heartbeat-interval` "0 disables"; `--max-buffer-bytes=0` = no orchestrator cap, engine default) — `max-buffer-bytes` / `apply-exec-timeout` / `heartbeat-interval` are now POINTER-typed in `SyncSpec` (nil = key omitted → the `sync start` flag default via the new `orDefault` helper; an explicit 0 passes through as 0, byte-identical to the flag; YAML key names unchanged); the `apply-retry-attempts`/`-backoff-base`/`-backoff-cap` trio is pointer-typed for the REFUSAL side of the same class (nil = omitted → ADR-0038 defaults; an explicit value INCLUDING 0 reaches `validateRetryFlags` verbatim and is refused with the CLI's exact out-of-range message, instead of being silently absorbed into the default); only the restart `backoff-base`/`backoff-cap` stay value-typed (`RestartPolicy.withDefaults` documents zero-as-unset and there is no CLI counterpart; the `printFleetPlan` coercion is display-only), with in-code comments. Pinned through the REAL parsers per the Bug-180 lesson: `TestFleetZeroDisables_ThroughLoadPath_N11` ({omitted → default; explicit `0` and `0s` → 0/disabled; non-zero → verbatim} × each "0 disables" field through `loadFleetConfig`), `TestFleetRetryZeroRefused_ThroughLoadPath_N11` (explicit `apply-retry-*: 0` refused through the load path with the CLI-identical message; omitted → defaults; in-range → verbatim), `TestSyncStartFleetParity_ExplicitZero_N11` (kong-parsed `sync start` explicit-0 and defaults produce the SAME Streamer values as the fleet keys), `TestSyncSpecFingerprint_ZeroVsOmitted_N11` (explicit 0 ≠ omitted under the SIGHUP-reload fingerprint, so flipping between them restarts the sync). *Original:* `cmd/sluice/sync_run.go:783-791` coerced `apply-exec-timeout: 0` / `heartbeat-interval: 0` / `max-buffer-bytes: 0` to the 60s/60s/64MiB defaults via `firstNonZero*`, while the flag help documents "0 disables" and `sync start` passes an explicit 0 through — "unset" and "explicit 0" were conflated for fleet specs only.
- ✅ **FIXED (in review, 2026-07-08) — pgtrigger cold-start anchor: in-flight-txn rows are MVCC-invisible to the anchor query (epoch-INDEPENDENT hole; live-confirmed 2026-07-08 during the N-1 xid8 fix).** `readChangeLogAnchor`'s `MIN(id)-1` hold-down arm can only see *visible* rows — a change-log row inserted by a still-open transaction is invisible to the anchor's snapshot, so when that txn's already-allocated id was lower than every visible not-yet-settled row, the anchor landed above it (repro: A inserts change-log id=1 open, B inserts id=2 committed → anchor 1, gap-free needs 0; the loss reproduced end-to-end through the real Streamer cold start — row missing on target, exit 0). **Fix (three-phase; Phase-A failing pins written first):** `OpenSnapshotStream` now exports the copy snapshot's visibility horizon from the pinned conn, assigns a txid upper bound on the pool (`pg_current_xact_id()`), waits for every pre-bound transaction to settle (fresh snapshot per poll; 5-min budget → loud refusal naming the stuck txids + pg_stat_activity remedy), then clamps the anchor below `MIN(id)` of change-log rows not `pg_visible_in_snapshot` in the horizon. **The candidate sketch here (pg_snapshot_xip alone) proved UNSOUND during Phase A** — snapshot xmax is latestCompletedXid+1, so the only running txn sits at/above xmax outside every xip list (live-probed `744:744:`); the shipped wait unions snapshot xmin (oldest still-running) with xip under the assigned bound. Invariant + case split documented on `waitForPreSnapshotTxnsToSettle` and in ADR-0066 impl-notes. Pins: `TestSnapshotStream_InFlightTxnAnchor_NoGap`, `TestPGTriggerStreamer_InFlightTxnSpansColdStart_NoLoss` (both mutation-verified: fail with the clamp disabled), `TestSettleWait_TimeoutRefusesLoudly`, `TestSettleWait_QuiescentSourceFirstPollExits` + query-shape unit pins. The narrower steady-state cousin (xid-assignment order can invert change-log-id order across multi-statement txns — inherent to the ADR's Debezium-style design; the safety-lag hold-back bounds it) is UNCHANGED and remains open.

### Open bugs awaiting fix windows

Tracked in detail in the project's internal regression catalog; recap here for roadmap visibility:

- ~~**VStream COPY silently display-rounds FLOAT columns (found 2026-07-09 ground-truthing the ADR-0153 G4 residual; MED-HIGH, silent-precision class, PlanetScale/Vitess sources only):**~~ **FIXED (2026-07-09; pending review/release) — post-COPY exact SQL re-read, EXACT by default on BOTH consumers.** Root cause: vttablet's rowstreamer issues a bare-column SELECT over the text protocol, so the wire bytes are mysqld's own FLOAT rendering (the exact bug class ADR-0153's `(col * 1E0)` projection fixed on the SQL reader — but that SELECT is built inside vttablet, un-injectable client-side, so the *reader stays rounded by design*; the fix lives one layer up). Ground truth on vttestserver mysql80: `8388608` → `8388610`, float32-max → a different float32, `-123456.789` → `-123457`. The CDC leg is float32-exact (pinned), DOUBLE + `-0.0` exact on both legs (pinned). **Fix:** a new `ir.LossyFloatCopyReader` gate (the VStream cold-start reader returns true) + an `ir.FloatRepairWriter` target surface (MySQL + PG). **Sync cold-start** (`internal/pipeline/streamer_coldstart_float_repair.go`): after the bulk-copy completes and BEFORE the CDC anchor is persisted, re-read every repairable table's single-precision FLOAT columns EXACTLY from the source over a separate SQL connection (`Engine.OpenRowReader` → the `(col*1E0)` projection) and UPDATE the target rows by PK; CDC then replays from the copy anchor forward, so any value that changed in the re-read window is re-applied to its final value (exact + eventually-consistent). **Backup** (`internal/pipeline/backup/float_repair.go`): also EXACT by default — a `floatExactPatchReader` wraps the snapshot reader, building a per-table PK→exact-floats map and patching each COPY row's FLOAT columns before archiving (a bounded merge-join is infeasible: the VStream COPY stream is NOT PK-ordered — Vitess scans by a cheaper unique key than the PK and re-emits catchup rows out of order, so there's no monotonic key to merge on). The map is **BOUNDED-memory**: capped at `--float-reread-max-rows` (default 2M rows; serial VStream sweep → one table at a time), and a table over the cap **falls back loudly** (default: WARN + rounded; `--strict-float`: refuse) rather than OOM-ing on a huge FLOAT table (ADR-0071 tenet). Cost = a bounded within-row temporal skew that self-heals on a chain restore (incrementals replay from the full's `EndPosition` forward); position/VGTID untouched. **Escape hatches (both paths):** `--no-float-exact-reread` (opt-out → rounded-but-perfectly-consistent) and `--strict-float` (refuse loudly, `SLUICE-E-VSTREAM-FLOAT-LOSSY`, exit 3). Keyless / float-PK-only tables can't be re-read → WARN-only rounded (or refuse under `--strict-float`). `TestVStream_FloatCarrierParity`'s skipped sub-test is converted to a reader-still-rounds ground-truth pin (the reader is unfixable); the target-exactness pins live at the pipeline layer (`TestStreamer_FloatRepair_*_VStream_PG`) + the writer/patch/plan unit + integration tests. Concurrency-critical (cold-start→CDC handoff ordering): the `-race` Integration + vstream jobs must gate the tag.
- ~~**`TestStreamer_PostgresToPostgres_BatchedApply` threshold flake (2026-07-09; LOW, CI-noise class)**~~ — **FIXED (2026-07-09; pending review/release), as the mechanism assertion the entry prescribed.** The pg_stat_database commit-delta constant (`<= 52`) is gone; the test now observes every coalesced flush through a new pipeline test seam (`batchApplyObserverForTest`, an [ir.BatchObserver] installed on the applier when the AIMD controller doesn't take the seat; onTableCopiedObserver disposition) and asserts the MECHANISM: every source row flowed through an observed flush AND mean rows/flush >= 10 (per-change apply yields mean exactly 1 — the per-change Apply path bypasses the batch loop and its observer entirely, so both assertions fail against it by an order of magnitude; healthy run = 2-3 flushes of ~100). The test pins ApplyConcurrency=1 (the seam watches the serial ADR-0092 batch loop; the ADR-0104 lane path reports to per-lane controllers and has its own suites). No timing-dependent constant remains. *Original:* flaked once on a loaded `-race` runner — 200 source rows landed in 55 dest commits vs the pinned `<= 52`; the assertion counted DEST COMMIT deltas, which depend on change-arrival timing against the coalescing window.
- **UNIQUE-constraint attribute fidelity (2026-07-04, from the TRIAGE-#4 review; LOW-MED, silent-weaker class):** `DEFERRABLE`, PG-15 `UNIQUE NULLS NOT DISTINCT` (`connullsnotdistinct`), and PG-17 `WITHOUT OVERLAPS` (`conperiod`) are read nowhere, so a constraint-backed unique carrying them lands *weaker* on the target (a NULLS-NOT-DISTINCT source admits duplicate NULLs going forward; WITHOUT OVERLAPS fails loudly at ADD CONSTRAINT only if the data happens to overlap). Pre-existing (the old demotion lost them too) but now behind a "full parity" claim. Fix shape: read the three pg_constraint attributes and either carry faithfully or refuse/WARN loudly per the house posture; seed the dump-parity oracle with all three shapes.
- **Sequence-carry review residuals (2026-07-03, both LOW, loud-not-silent):** (a) `primeOneStandaloneSequence`'s never-called canonicalization (`srcLast = Value − Increment`) can push the cutover prime past the *inner* bound when `Increment > margin` (e.g. `START 1000 INCREMENT 5000`, never called) — `setval` errors and cutover fails loudly with a raw PG bounds error; clamping applyValue into `[MinValue, MaxValue]` on both sides would turn the confusing abort into a correct prime. (b) Mid-stream `ALTER SEQUENCE` option changes (e.g. INCREMENT) produce no SchemaDelta (`diffSchemas` is table-only, pre-existing) — the new end-of-window refresh *records* the changed options in the newest link but the chain-tail re-prime only setvals, never ALTERs, so option drift is recorded-but-unapplied on a restored target.
- **Identity sequences go stale at chain-restore tail** (found 2026-07-03 during the item-51 sequence-carry review; live-reproduced: `duplicate key value violates unique constraint "orders_pkey" (SQLSTATE 23505)` on the first post-restore insert). ✅ **FIXED 2026-07-04 (replay-path hardening chunk):** `ChainRestore.Run` step 5 now calls `syncIdentitySequencesAtTail` right beside the item-51 standalone-sequence re-prime — the newest link's schema snapshot, retargeted + filtered like the base full's restore, through the required `ir.SchemaWriter.SyncIdentitySequences` surface (engine-neutral: no-op on MySQL/SQLite) under the ADR-0114 reparent retry. Idempotent, data-derived MAX+1; the broker's `--reset-target-data` ChainRestore inherits it. Pinned by `TestBackup_ChainRestore_IdentitySequenceSyncedAtTail` (the exact 23505 repro, first post-restore insert must draw max+1) + `TestChainRestore_IdentitySequencesSyncedAtTail_Dispatch` (unit: sync runs twice — base full + tail, tail last).
- **SYSTEMIC — cross-engine out-of-range / invalid values silently transformed (4 vectors)** (found 2026-06-08, rig systemic sweep of v0.99.18; rig `FINDING-systemic-out-of-range-silent-loss.md`). A value the target can't faithfully hold is silently clamped/truncated/normalized to a wrong-but-plausible value with exit 0, instead of refused. **Operator decisions (2026-06-08):** Vector A → refuse loudly by default + opt-in `--zero-date={error,null,epoch}`; Vector D → keep TINYINT(1)→bool but WARN on non-{0,1} + add integer override tokens.
  - **Vector A (CRITICAL, default path, ✅ FIXED v0.99.19):** MySQL invalid/zero/partial dates (`0000-00-00`, `YYYY-00-00`, `YYYY-MM-00`) silently normalized to wrong dates (e.g. `2026-00-00`→`2025-11-30`). Root: `cfg.ParseTime=true` (`connect.go:205`) → go-sql-driver parses partial dates via `time.Date` (which normalizes) *before* sluice's `decodeTime` sees them, so the original is lost. **Fix shipped:** rather than flip `ParseTime` (TZ-risky), the read path reads `DATE`/`DATETIME`/`TIMESTAMP` via `CAST(... AS CHAR)` (`selectColumnExpr`, used by both `buildSelect` and `buildBatchedSelect`) so `decodeTime` validates the raw string. Zero/partial dates surface as a `*zeroDateValueError` sentinel, resolved at the reader sites (which hold `col.Nullable`) by `applyZeroDatePolicy` per `--zero-date={error,null,epoch}` (default `error`). `SetZeroDateMode` mirrors `sessionSQLMode`. Pinned: full temporal class × every zero shape × each policy (unit) + live-driver normalization ground-truth (integration, real MySQL 8.0). Behavior change: `0000-00-00` previously → NULL silently, now refused by default (`--zero-date=null` restores). Docs: `migrating-legacy-mysql.md` §1, `value-types.md`. **Value-fidelity review follow-ups (2026-06-08):** (1) ✅ FIXED — the `CAST(... AS CHAR) AS \`c\`` projection aliases a temporal PK to its bare name, so `buildBatchedSelect`'s `ORDER BY \`c\`` bound the CHAR alias (string sort) while the keyset predicate `(\`c\`) > (?)` compared the date column; correct only by ISO lexical monotonicity and it forced a filesort. Now both clauses are table-qualified (`\`tbl\`.\`c\``) → date-typed, index-ordered; pinned by a SQL-shape unit test + DATE/DATETIME(6)-PK pagination integration tests + a chunked-path zero-date integration test. (2) ✅ FIXED v0.99.19 — **VStream parity:** the PlanetScale/Vitess CDC parser `parseVStreamDateTime` (`cdc_vstream.go`) now detects zero/partial dates via the shared `isMySQLZeroDate` and returns the `*zeroDateValueError` sentinel (instead of a generic `time.Parse` error → raw `[]byte` passthrough → confusing downstream failure). `decodeVStreamCell` surfaces the sentinel as the cell value (it has no error channel); `decodeVStreamRow` resolves it via `applyZeroDatePolicy` — refuse (default) errors the stream loudly naming the column, null carries SQL NULL (refused on a NOT NULL field, derived from `query.Field.Flags` NOT_NULL with assume-nullable fallback), epoch substitutes the representable floor. Covers the live CDC reader + the cold-start COPY + CDC catch-up paths. Pinned: `TestDecodeVStreamCell_ZeroDateSentinel` (family × zero shapes; valid→time.Time; malformed→[]byte) + `TestDecodeVStreamRow_ZeroDatePolicy` (refuse/null/epoch/NOT-NULL). `--zero-date` now behaves identically on the vanilla MySQL and PlanetScale/Vitess source paths.
  - **Vector D (HIGH, default path, ALL directions incl same-engine, ✅ FIXED v0.99.21):** MySQL `TINYINT(1)` mapped to bool at the IR read layer → non-{0,1} values (2/127/−1/−128) silently collapsed to true/false, corrupting even MySQL→MySQL. **Fix shipped:** kept the `TINYINT(1)`→bool default (documented MySQL convention) but the bulk-copy / snapshot read path now DETECTS any value ∉ {0,1} and WARNs loudly **once per column** (`boolRangeWarner` in `bool_range_warn.go`, gated in `RowReader.stream`; pure detector `tinyBoolOutOfRange` in `value_decode.go`), naming the `table.column` + an example value + the `--type-override` remedy. Added `smallint`/`integer`/`int` target-type tokens (`translate/mappings.go` registry → `ir.Integer{16/32}`); the override rewrites the IR type the **reader** decodes with, so the cell is read as an integer (not collapsed) and preserved end-to-end — `smallint` is the safe floor (a `tinyint` override would re-emit `TINYINT(1)` and re-trigger the bool mapping). Pinned: `tinyBoolOutOfRange` purity + warn-once unit tests; token resolution; an end-to-end integration test (MySQL→PG default warns+collapses; MySQL→PG **and** same-engine MySQL→MySQL override preserves real SMALLINT values). Docs: `type-mapping.md`, `value-types.md`. **WARN coverage now spans ALL read paths (v0.99.21 follow-up landed):** the copy/snapshot reader (`RowReader.stream`), the binlog CDC reader (`decodeBinlogRow`, via a `boolWarn` on `CDCReader`), and the VStream CDC + cold-start-COPY path (`decodeVStreamRow`, via a `boolWarn` on `vstreamCDCReader` / `vstreamSnapshotStream`; VStream cells are text-encoded so the detector re-parses the literal). Each warner is per-reader, warn-once-per-`table.column`, nil-safe. Pinned by `TestDecodeBinlogRow_TinyInt1OutOfRangeWarns` + `TestDecodeVStreamRow_TinyInt1OutOfRangeWarns`. No remaining Vector-D detection gap.
  - **Vector B (HIGH, requires `--mysql-sql-mode=''`): ✅ FIXED v0.99.28.** Overflow/over-long/out-of-range on a MySQL-target write under `--mysql-sql-mode=''` → silent clamp/truncate. **Ground-truthed** (rig MySQL): under `sql_mode=''` the value silently clamps (300→127, 'toolong'→'too', 99999→999) but MySQL STILL flags it on the warning list (`@@warning_count`/`SHOW WARNINGS`) — so the "non-strict suppresses the warnings" assumption was wrong; the signal is there, the prior code just SKIPPED checking it under relaxed mode. **Fix:** `reportBulkWriteWarnings` (`load_data_writer.go`) now, under relaxed mode, emits a loud **one-time-per-table WARN** (not a refusal — the operator opted into coercion) naming the coercions + the `--type-override` remedy, instead of the silent skip; under strict mode it still refuses. Wired into ALL THREE bulk-write paths (the Bug-74 path-family lesson — a value-fidelity review BLOCK caught that the first cut covered only two): LOAD DATA (`writeLoadData`), the batched-INSERT path (`writeBatched`, used when `local_infile=OFF`/geometry), AND the idempotent upsert path (`writeBatchedIdempotent`, used on **resume / parallel chunked copy >100k / add-table / VStream cold-start** — the path most large migrations take). Each pins a single conn so the session-scoped `SHOW WARNINGS` is reliable; the idempotent path checks before advancing the durable watermark so a strict-mode refusal can't mark a clamped batch durable. **Bonus:** reading `SHOW WARNINGS` FIRST (the old code read `@@warning_count` first, which clears the list) fixes the empty-`Examples: []` cosmetic bug in the strict-mode refusal AND the NaN/±Inf refusal. Pinned: `TestLoadDataWarning_RelaxedModeWarnsNotRefuses` + `TestWriteBatched_RelaxedModeWarnsOnClamp` + `TestWriteBatchedIdempotent_RelaxedModeWarnsOnClamp` (clamp 300→127 + WARN, once-per-table) + the strict refuse pin retained. **Remaining (minor, not a bulk-copy gap):** the CDC applier write path (steady-state out-of-range under relaxed mode) doesn't yet run this check; all THREE migrate/cold-start bulk-copy paths — the dominant surface — are covered.
  - **Vector C (MEDIUM, no silent loss):** no override token to a fitting type. `uint64` decimal path **FIXED** (`190ce50`), `datetime` token **FIXED** (`b8d7218`), `smallint`/`integer`/`int` tokens added for Vector D (v0.99.21). **embedded-NUL → PG text: FIXED v0.99.25** — a string carrying a NUL byte (`0x00`) bound for a PG `text`/`varchar`/`char` column is now refused loudly at `prepareValue` (`postgres/row_writer.go`) naming the column + the data-preserving remedy (`--type-override COL=bytea`), instead of pgx failing opaquely mid-COPY with SQLSTATE 22021 (a MySQL CHAR/VARCHAR/TEXT can hold embedded NULs; PG text cannot). No value silently altered (stripping the NUL would be silent corruption). Pinned `TestPrepareValueNULByteRefused` (text/varchar/char + DOMAIN-recursion + bytea-OK + NUL-free passthrough). **FIXED follow-ups:** (a) ✅ MySQL `TIME` duration (−838:59:59…838:59:59) → PG `INTERVAL` (v0.99.26) — new `ir.Interval` type (TierExtension) + `interval` override token; MySQL reads the column as its textual duration, PG emits `INTERVAL` and bulk-loads it via the batched-INSERT (text) path (pgx binary COPY can't encode a string→interval, so `tableHasIntervalColumn` routes it like the verbatim path); a MySQL/non-PG target refuses loudly (emitColumnType + `unsupportablePGtoMySQL`). Backup envelope round-trips it. Pinned end-to-end (838:59:59 / -12:30:00 / 00:00:05 → real PG interval, exact) + MySQL-target refusal. (b) ✅ `decimal(p,s)`/`numeric(p,s)`/`varchar(n)` paren CLI shorthand (v0.99.26) — and it turned out the old `decimal:precision=N,scale=M` hint **never parsed from the CLI** (only YAML `target_type_options`), so this is the first working CLI precision-bearing decimal; all the range-overflow advisories were corrected to the working `decimal(N,M)` form. Remaining Vector C: embedded-NUL **FIXED** (v0.99.25). Nothing left in Vector C except the broader Vector B silent-clamp gate (separate item below).
- **MySQL `BIGINT UNSIGNED` > 2^63−1 has NO working migration path to PG + the remediation hint is broken** (**FIXED `190ce50`, 2026-06-08** — `decodeDecimal`/`decodeString` carry uint64/int64 as exact text + the notice points at `--type-override COL=decimal:precision=20,scale=0`; unit + integration pinned). _(Original write-up retained for traceability.)_ Found 2026-06-08 on the v0.99.18 rig value-fidelity sweep. **No silent loss** — every path fails loud (exit≠0, 0 rows) — but it blocks a legitimate common migration (unsigned-64 IDs/counters/bitfields) and the *documented recovery path does not function*. Two confirmed defects: **(1) the MySQL value reader can't decode a `uint64` driver value for non-integer IR targets** — `decodeDecimal` (`value_decode.go:157`) and `decodeString` (`value_decode.go:181`) handle only `[]byte`/`string`, so `--type-override COL=decimal|text` fails `cannot decode uint64 as {Decimal|string}`; **(2) the unsigned-bigint notice's remediation is wrong** (`translate/unsigned_bigint.go:163` says `--type-override TABLE.COL=numeric`, but `numeric` is not a recognized override token — only `decimal` is — and `decimal` yields `numeric(10,0)`, too few digits for a 20-digit value). **Fix sketch:** add `uint64`/`int64` cases to `decodeDecimal`+`decodeString` (carry as exact decimal/text via `strconv.Format{Uint,Int}`); default an unsigned-64 `decimal` override to `numeric(20,0)` not `(10,0)`; correct the notice to name a token that exists *and* works end-to-end (or point at the YAML `mappings:` form if only YAML can set `numeric(20,0)` precision). **Pin:** MySQL→PG migrate of a `BIGINT UNSIGNED` column holding `2^64−1` must land the exact value via the documented override. Full write-up: rig `FINDING-uint64-no-migration-path.md` (2026-06-08).
- **NaN/±Inf refusal message has an empty `Examples: []` list** — ✅ **FIXED v0.99.28 (a bonus of the Vector B refactor).** Root cause: the LOAD-DATA-warning guard read `SELECT @@warning_count` BEFORE `SHOW WARNINGS`, and that intervening SELECT clears MySQL's diagnostic list, so `SHOW WARNINGS` returned nothing and `Examples` rendered empty. `reportBulkWriteWarnings` now reads `SHOW WARNINGS` first (one query → count + detail), so the refusal (NaN/±Inf and any other LOAD-DATA warning) names the offending values. (Found 2026-06-08 value-fidelity sweep probe #3.)
- **FINDING (corrected to LOW-MED after rig ground-truth — `sync` slot-loss recovery, found 2026-06-08 writing the ADR-0075 Phase 2b nit-#2 pin).** Initial in-tree test made this look like a 🔴 HIGH silent-loss (re-cold-start "didn't re-converge"); the **rig regression on the released v0.99.28 binary corrected that** — it is **NOT silent loss on the default path**. Slot-loss restart (PG failover on PG<17, or `pg_drop_replication_slot`): the ErrPositionInvalid fall-through fires correctly (`streamer.go:1499` → `coldStartMultiDatabase`), then the **Bug-9 cold-start preflight REFUSES LOUDLY (exit 1)** — `cold-start refused: target table "…" already contains data … warm-resume isn't possible either` — non-zero exit, never reaches CDC, target untouched. **Loud-failure-tenet-compliant.** The single-DB streamer equivalent behaves identically. (My in-tree test "failed" because it asserted re-convergence and polled the target, instead of checking the returned refusal error — test-expectation bug, not a product bug; the test was removed.) **Residual (LOW-MED, OPEN):** `--force-cold-start` BYPASSES the Bug-9 preflight, so on slot-loss-with-populated-target it could re-copy/not-converge without the loud gate — narrower (requires the operator to explicitly pass the flag). **UX item (LOW, optional):** on slot-loss recovery the loud refusal forces operator intervention (`--reset-target-data` for a clean re-copy); an idempotent re-converge would be friendlier but isn't required (refuse is loud + safe). **Pin to add:** slot-loss restart → assert the loud refusal (`Run` returns the "already contains data" error), the actual contract — NOT re-convergence.
- **Bug 17** (deferred until a real schema hits it; **not** a silent-loss class) — a narrow `impact_items`-shape cross-engine COALESCE the auto-translator doesn't rewrite. The common bool/int COALESCE shapes DO translate (v0.8.0→v0.10.1); this residual fails **loud** (target parse rejection) and has the working `--expr-override` escape hatch (its test fixture is `impact_items.is_cleared=coalesce(x,0)`). Closing it means open-ended translator-catalog breadth with zero current demand — fold into item 5's demand-gated translator rules. _(Reviewed 2026-06-08: explicitly deferred over the multi-version sweep — loud-failure + escape hatch, not correctness.)_
- **Bug 25** (deferred until a real schema hits it; **not** a silent-loss class) — the enum-typed STORED gencol case is FIXED (TEXT + CHECK, `postgres/ddl_emit.go:490+`). The residual is the broader **STABLE-not-IMMUTABLE function in a STORED gencol** class (`TO_CHAR`/`CONCAT_WS`/`extract(epoch …)`/`DATE_FORMAT`), documented per-function in `translator-coverage.md`. It fails **loud** at apply time and has the `--expr-override` escape hatch; the real fixes (a STABLE-function pre-flight catalog, or trigger-based gencols — semantic-gaps `path (b)`) are open-ended + demand-gated. _(Reviewed 2026-06-08: deferred over the sweep — no clean small slice, no demand.)_
- **Bug 26** — PostGIS SRID dropped on schema translation. *Closed in v0.28.0 (ADR-0035).*
- **Bug 27** — VStream POINT bytes mis-parsed. *Closed in v0.28.0 (ADR-0035) at the unit-test layer; end-to-end verification on the local self-hosted Vitess cluster (`vitesscluster` tag, item 1(e)) — the cheaper replacement for the originally-deferred `psverify` real-PlanetScale leg.*
- **Bug 41** — PG CDC decode crash on UUID columns. *Closed in v0.21.2.*
- **Bug 42** — cross-engine PG → MySQL `DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` translator gap. *Closed in v0.23.1.* `pgToMySQLDefaultExpr` in `internal/engines/mysql/ddl_emit.go` carries `gen_random_uuid()` → `(UUID())` and `random()` → `(RAND())`.
- **Bug 44** — same-engine MySQL `DEFAULT (UUID())` / `(RAND())` lost outer parens. *Closed in v0.23.2.* `wrapMySQLExpressionDefault` helper in `internal/engines/mysql/ddl_emit.go` covers the function-call shape; bare `CURRENT_TIMESTAMP[(N)]` and already-wrapped forms pass through.
- **Bug 47** — `{}` → `[]` on MySQL targets when default JSON cast surfaces via cross-engine. *Closed in v0.29.1 (initial fix) + v0.29.1 v2 (proper upstream disambiguation).*
- **Bug 51** — PG `geography(POINT, srid)` widened to `geography(Geometry, srid)` due to mixed-case `geography_columns.type`. *Closed in v0.33.2.*
- **Bug 52** — PG `geometry(POINTZ, srid)` Z/M/ZM dimensional variants lost on emit. *Closed in v0.33.3 (partial in v0.33.2, full closure via `coord_dimension` capture in v0.33.3).*
- **Bug 53** — PostGIS `coord_dimension` not captured in schema reader. *Closed in v0.33.3 (same release as Bug 52 full closure).*
- **Bug 64** — `DEFAULT` expression backtick leak on cross-engine MySQL → PG. *Closed in v0.66.1.*
- **Bug 65** — same-engine PG → PG expression-index `gin_trgm_ops` opclass survival. *Closed in v0.66.0.*
- **Bug 66** — multi-segment backup with absent `lineage.json` silently restored only the chain root. *Closed in v0.67.1.*
- **Bug 68** — PG multi-dimensional array column silently lost all rows on cross-engine PG → MySQL. *Closed in v0.69.0.*
- **Bug 69** — unconstrained PG `numeric`/`numeric[]` mis-emit. *Closed in v0.69.1.*
- **Bug 70** — NULL element inside any typed PG array hard-fails the PG → PG COPY-protocol writer. *Closed in v0.69.3.*
- **Bug 71** — PG `timetz` mis-mapped to `time` (OID 1083) and rejected at COPY encode. *Closed in v0.71.0.*
- **Bug 72** — wide PG `varchar(N)` emitted literally as MySQL `VARCHAR(N)` and not down-mapped to TEXT/MEDIUMTEXT. *Closed in v0.71.0.*
- **Bug 95** — backup chain rotation not born-contiguous (compaction blocker). *Closed in v0.88.0 (ADR-0067).*
- **Bug 96** — ext-owned-relation exclusion gap on cross-engine PG → MySQL. *Closed in v0.89.0.*
- **Bug 108** — CLI-overrides-YAML silent failure on redaction rules. *Closed in v0.96.0.*
- **Bug 110** — incremental backup's end-position schema-read scope. *Closed in v0.94.0.*
- **Bug 112** — PG table-RENAME mid-CDC stream silently drops subsequent writes. *Closed in v0.93.0.*
- **Bug 113** — PG DOMAIN-typed columns silently unwrap to base type (and CHECK lost). *Closed across v0.95.1 (loud-refuse) → v0.95.2/v0.95.3 (PG → PG round-trip carry) → v0.96.2 (PG → MySQL WARN) → v0.97.0 (PG → MySQL inline-CHECK on 8.0.16+) → v0.97.1 (regex backslash byte-fidelity).*
- **Bug 114** — PG migrate partial-failure leaves earlier tables without secondary indexes (no recovery hint). *Closed in v0.96.1.*
- **Bug 115** — non-default core PG opclasses dropped silently. *Closed in v0.95.0.*
- **Bug 116** — manifest `FormatVersion=1` silently drops security metadata on older sluice restore. *Closed in v0.94.1.*
- **Bug 117** — per-chunk encryption mode silently accepts a rotated passphrase between full and incremental. *Closed across v0.94.1 (verify-path probe) → v0.96.3 (incremental/stream ingestion-path probe).*
- **Bug 118** — PG `pg_lsn` / `txid_snapshot` CDC apply crash. *Re-verified closed in v0.94.1 cycle (likely already closed by v0.92.4's verbatim-type wire-encoding fix).*
- **Bug 119** — `ALTER TABLE ... DROP COLUMN` mid-CDC stream silently leaves the dropped column on the destination. *Closed in v0.93.0.*
- **Bug 120** — `DROP TABLE` + `CREATE TABLE <same-name>` mid-CDC stream silently drops every subsequent write. *Closed in v0.93.0.*
- **Bug 122** — `ir.Domain` value codec dispatch missing on PG row stream. *Closed in v0.95.3.*

UUID PK support across cross-engine restore is fully landed: Bug 41 (CDC value decode) + Bug 42 (schema-side default translation, PG → MySQL) + Bug 44 (same-engine MySQL function-call default wrapping) + v0.11.3's Bugs 28/29 (the MySQL → PG direction). All four corners covered for modern PG schemas (Rails, Django, Hasura, Supabase).

### MySQL & PlanetScale parity tracker

Sluice's recent feature work has cadenced PG-first; MySQL/PlanetScale parity is intentional but tracked. One-stop summary of what's PG-only today and where the MySQL/PS follow-up lives:

| PG-shipped feature | MySQL parity status | Tracked at |
|---|---|---|
| Phase 6.1 passphrase encryption (v0.22.0) | Engine-neutral — applies to both already | n/a |
| Phase 6.2 AWS KMS encryption (v0.23.0) | Engine-neutral — applies to both already | n/a |
| Mid-stream live add-table (`--no-drain`, v0.24.0) | Both engines, v0.27.0 — MySQL via streamer-side filter-flip (ADR-0034) | "Recently landed: Mid-stream add-table — MySQL Phase 2" |
| Multi-source aggregation `--target-schema` (v0.25.0) | Server-wide fan-out SHIPPED — multi-database MySQL (`--all-databases`/`--include-database`/`--exclude-database`, ADR-0074, v0.99.16) + multi-schema PG (ADR-0075, v0.99.24). Residual: the per-table `--rename-table` map (still deferred — DSN-choice workaround documented) | "Multi-source aggregation — MySQL native parity" entry above |
| Phase 2 strict zero-loss correctness (PG, closed v0.32.0 via ADR-0036) | PG-specific (pgoutput decode-time publication semantics) — MySQL Phase 2 has its own correctness story | "Recently landed: Mid-stream live add-table — strict zero-loss correctness (v0.32.0)" |
| GEOMETRY / SPATIAL support (v0.28.0, ADR-0035) | Both engines — PG → MySQL geometry round-trip with SRID preserved; VStream POINT prefix stripped (Bug 27); cross-engine refusal lifted | "Recently landed: GEOMETRY / SPATIAL — PostGIS-aware translation" |
| `--type-override`, `--expr-override`, translator catalog | Both engines, both directions | n/a |
| Index-build overlap (PG target, v0.99.x, ADR-0077) | Both engines — MySQL-target overlap SHIPPED v0.99.30 (ADR-0080) + combined-`ALTER` follow-up (`591da65`); PlanetScale/Vitess targets decline and defer to platform online-DDL. Measured −13% median / −21% best-case wall at index-heavy MySQL→MySQL scale (`benchmarks/mysql/`) | item 3c above |

PlanetScale-specific tracking:

| PlanetScale concern | Status | Tracked at |
|---|---|---|
| Bug 27 VStream POINT bytes prefix | Closed in v0.28.0 (ADR-0035) at the unit-test layer; end-to-end verification on the local self-hosted Vitess cluster (`vitesscluster` tag, item 1(e)) — replaces the deferred `psverify` real-PlanetScale leg | "Recently landed: GEOMETRY / SPATIAL — PostGIS-aware translation" |
| Mid-stream Phase 2.5 (VStream-specific add-table mechanism) | Demand-driven follow-on to v0.27.0's MySQL Phase 2; VStream is a separate code path from vanilla MySQL binlog | (no roadmap entry yet — track here when demand surfaces) |
| PlanetScale Postgres slot lifecycle (Patroni-managed; silent loss on failover without `Logical slot name` config) | Documented in `docs/postgres-source-prep.md`; not exercised in default CI | "PlanetScale MySQL+Vitess test-matrix expansion" entry above |
| Broader VStream coverage (cross-shard PK, geometry edge cases, slot recovery) | Operator-run via the `psverify` build tag (requires PlanetScale credentials); not in default CI | "PlanetScale MySQL+Vitess test-matrix expansion" entry above |

### Bug 27 (closed in v0.28.0)

Closed by ADR-0035 — VStream's `query.Type_GEOMETRY` cell decoder now strips the 4-byte little-endian SRID prefix before delivering bytes downstream, matching the vanilla MySQL driver path (`cdc_vstream.go:1354`). End-to-end verification runs against the local self-hosted Vitess cluster (`vitesscluster` build tag, roadmap item 1(e)): a `POINT` column is seeded, streamed via `FlavorVitess`, and the decoded WKB is asserted SRID-stripped against MySQL `ST_AsWKB`. This is the cheaper replacement for the originally-deferred `psverify` leg (no PlanetScale credentials required); the `psverify` spot-check remains available for operators who want to confirm against real hosted PlanetScale. See [ADR-0035](adr/adr-0035-postgis-geometry-spatial-support.md).

### Performance frontier (2026-06-12 profiling round — where the remaining time actually goes)

Two evidence rounds on v0.99.41-era main; profiles under `workspace/pprof-migrate-v09941/`
(gitignored), experiment logs in sluice-testing `workspace/perfB/`:

- **PG→PG migrate (raw-copy lane) is wire-bound, not compute-bound.** pprof on
  the 136 GB rig: sluice on-CPU ~6% of wall; the ADR-0078 passthrough does zero
  per-row work (0 flat samples in sluice functions; no steady-state allocs; no
  lock contention; `--table-parallelism=1` has the identical CPU shape). The
  only sluice-reducible item is the reader→writer `io.Pipe` memmove at <0.5% of
  wall. **Consequence: the positional-`ir.Row` rewrite (repo-audit P3) is NOT
  justified by this lane** — if it pays anywhere it's the cross-engine typed
  lane (TOAST/wide-row corpus differential is the test that would decide).
- **MySQL-target migrate sits at the InnoDB server floor.** sluice's LOAD DATA
  path (already 8-way parallel within-table via ADR-0019 chunking) matches a
  hand-run `LOAD DATA LOCAL INFILE` to rig noise (~95k vs ~98k rows/s on the
  1M-row anchor); InnoDB single-table clustered-PK ingest does not parallelize
  (1×/4×/8× concurrent loaders all ≈100k) and is ingest-bound, not commit-bound
  (`innodb_flush_log_at_trx_commit=2` ≈ +5%). **No Go-side or parallelism lever
  moves this number; myloader faces the same wall.** Per-direction tracking +
  the full numbers: sluice-testing `THROUGHPUT.md` (#34).
- **10k-tiny-tables (decides #56, measured 2026-06-12 — sluice-testing
  `workspace/perfC/VERDICTS.md`): sluice ≈13 ms/table vs pgcopydb ≈128 ms/table
  on the same corpus — sluice is ~10× AHEAD on this shape**, so the tiny-table
  batch lane is demand-gated, not perf-gated: do not build without a real user
  hitting it. The future lever, should demand appear, is precise: ~80% of wall
  is the serial CREATE TABLE phase (one network round-trip per table,
  `internal/engines/postgres/schema_writer.go:288-296`, flat across
  `--table-parallelism` which only governs bulk_copy) — a batch lane must
  batch DDL statements per round-trip, not COPY.
- **Wide-row typed lane (decides positional-`ir.Row`, audit P3 — same round):
  do NOT schedule the XL rewrite.** On a 750k × ~4.2 KB/row MySQL→PG copy
  (~200 MB/s, 8-way), the typed lane is 22.5% on-CPU and driver-dominated:
  pgx binary COPY-encode 42%, read/scan ~30%, sluice-owned typed-lane ~15% of
  which the `ir.Row` map cost (`copy_source.go:68` per-column lookup + value
  boxing) is ~8-9%. A perfect positional rewrite addresses single-digit CPU —
  far below the XL bar. Re-open only on separately-measured GC pressure at
  high concurrency.
- Remaining measured frontier worth a future chunk: backup-path zstd (32% of
  backup CPU post-codec — level sweep / parallel chunk compression).
